Drug Trafficking Korean

Violently Assaults Beiping City Police

Police Chief Bai Changhui Injured

(Beiping) Since the promulgation of the Beiping City Anti-Drug Regulations, the Public Security Bureau has ordered its subordinates to vigorously search for drug offenders. Koreans in Beiping City have recently felt that they cannot sell drugs, so they are venting their anger on the local authorities. Last night, at No. 10 Daxihu Tong, Nanshuncheng Street, Fuchengmen Inner City, a Korean named Zhang Shizhe, who has always been in charge of selling white powder in the Xicheng area and earning a very good income, summoned more than 20 Korean colleagues after hearing that the police have been strictly arresting drug offenders recently and that addicts are hesitant to come forward. They bound two people who were going to buy white powder. A Korean went to the fourth section of the fourth district to report a robbery. Bai Changhui, the police chief of the section, led police officers such as Cheng Yongli to the courtyard. Zhang ordered the Koreans holding poles to beat Bai and others. Police Chief Bai and others dodged while blowing whistles to call for help. Soon, police officers stationed at Fuchengmen came to their aid. Director Deng Zhenzhong also rushed to the scene after hearing the report. Bai Changhui and Cheng Yongli had been hit in the head, back, flanks, arms, and other places, and their clothing had also been torn. They were taken to the station to recover. The two men who were bound, Zhao and Xiao, were taken to the station for strict interrogation. Yu Jinhe, Director of the Public Security Bureau, has reported the matter to the Municipal Government and requested instructions. (Special dispatch on the 19th)

Boundary Demarcation Issue Between Two Counties on the Hebei-Shandong Border

(Jinan) The conference of representatives from Hebei's Yanshan and Shandong's Wudi counties to demarcate the boundary has failed three times. It will be submitted to the administrative and judicial counties for resolution. (Special dispatch on the 19th)

Building a Dam on the Yongding River

Causes a Conflict Among Villagers

(Beiping) The upper section of the fourth section of the south bank of the Yongding River is under the jurisdiction of Liangxiang County, and the north bank is under the jurisdiction of the third district of Wanping County. The villagers on the south bank, because the dam had been in disrepair for many years, obtained permission from the Yongding River Affairs Bureau to build a dam. The villagers gathered more than 50 people on the 12th of this month and began the work of building the embankment. At 2:00 PM on the 13th, while they were working on the riverbank, many people on the north bank suddenly shot at the south bank with rifles. Many people were injured and the rest hid on the ground. The gunshots were dense, about 300 rounds, and the situation was serious. Zhang Zhongyi, the section chief in charge, sent many river soldiers to protect the work. The villagers tried to escape to the section office to hide and sent people to nearby villages on the north bank to inquire about the truth. According to reports, the shooters had fled. It was said that they were villagers from Caogezhuang in the third district of Wanping County who held a meeting to oppose the damming of the south bank to prevent flooding on the north bank. Therefore, they shot and used force to stop it and agreed to persevere to the end. The villagers on the south bank have submitted a request to the Yongding River Affairs Bureau and the governments of Liangxiang and Wanping counties, requesting instructions on how to handle the aftermath. (Special dispatch on the 19th)

Shortage of Rice and Salt in Ting City

Chen Peikun Cables the Province for Relief

(Fuzhou) Chen Peikun, chairman of the Provincial Relief Committee, telegraphed the province from Longyan: (1) He plans to purchase 5,000 bags of rice and requests the province to telegraph the Sui Jinggong Office to borrow 10 vehicles from the transportation team to transport the rice to Ting City in ten days. (2) Ting City is short of salt. Please consult with the Salt Transportation Office to allocate 100,000 catties of salt to be handed over to the Zhangzhou Chamber of Commerce to find a way to transport it to Longyan and distribute it to Changting, Liancheng, and other counties for sale at a fair price. The salt fees will be gradually paid by the Relief Committee. Chen also plans to go to Ting City with Kang Shaozhou in the coming days and then return to the province. Kang will handle the relief affairs in Ting City thereafter. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 19th)

Salt Monopoly Issue

(Nanjing) Regarding the issue of salt monopoly, the Salt Affairs Administration of the Ministry of Finance originally planned to hold a salt affairs reform conference before the end of the year to discuss specific measures. However, while the monopoly plan is theoretically beneficial to the reform of salt administration, the various factual problems of salt transport, sales management, and anti-smuggling have been deeply rooted for a long time, making the implementation of the monopoly extremely difficult. At the same time, the Fifth Plenary Session has decided to establish a Salt Administration Reform Committee within a month, with the Minister of Finance as the ex officio chairman. In the future, the committee will have concrete discussions on salt administration reform matters. Therefore, regarding the plan to convene a salt administration conference within the year, it was decided to wait for the Reform Committee to conduct careful discussions, and the opinions of the salt affairs agencies of the ministry will be sent to the committee for research. No further discussions will be held separately. (Special dispatch on the 19th)

Joint Meeting of Various Indemnity Fund Organizations to Be Held Today

(Nanjing) The third joint meeting of various Indemnity Fund organizations is scheduled to be held at the Executive Yuan at 3:00 PM on the 20th. The estimated budgets for educational and cultural undertakings for 1934 from each organization have been sent to the meeting for review. (Special dispatch on the 19th)

(Nanjing) The joint meeting of various Indemnity Fund organizations is scheduled to be held on the 20th. The Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Education, and the Rural Reconstruction Committee all have proposals. The Executive Yuan is requesting an allocation to subsidize vocational education. The Rural Reconstruction Committee is requesting an allocation of 10% of each type of indemnity fund to run rural undertakings. The Ministry of Education is requesting an allocation to prepare border education, to subsidize the establishment of research institutes in national universities, and to allocate funds to establish a vocational school. (Special dispatch on the 19th)

Our Measures for Reducing League of Nations Dues

(Nanjing) According to diplomatic circles, after Hu Shize, our representative to the League of Nations, and Xiao Jirong, acting charge d'affaires of the French Embassy, submitted a memorandum to the League of Nations requesting a reduction in dues, results have now been obtained. It is said that the method for reducing dues is that China's dues will be reduced from 48 units to 42 units. According to 42 units, the amount is 1,200,000 Swiss francs, equivalent to 1,200,000 national currency. As for the accumulated arrears, they have been newly determined and will be paid off in 30 years, with each payment being 258,904.46 Swiss francs, equivalent to over 258,900 national currency. Therefore, starting next year, our country will pay a total of approximately 1,450,000 national currency per year for dues and repayment of arrears. (Special dispatch on the 19th)

London Pays Attention to China's Silver Problem

(London) According to the London Financial News, the suggestion made by Sir Sassoon in Shanghai yesterday to solve the silver problem was welcomed by the local market. However, it is felt that the United States may not change its silver policy and act accordingly. The Financial News believes that if the United States does not change its policy to accommodate Chinese interests, China will eventually be forced to devalue its currency in order to protect its trade and avoid the contractionary effects of expensive silver. However, according to Reuters' inquiries, the British in financial circles generally expect that China will not devalue its currency. However, the Americans' opinions on this are not so absolute. Some people also say that China will eventually adopt the pound sterling standard, because China cannot control silver, so using silver as a monetary basis is very unreliable. (Reuters dispatch on the 19th)

Japanese Deputy Consul Tanaka in Nanjing Temporarily Assumes Charge

(Nanjing) The Japanese Consul General in Nanjing, Suma, has returned to Japan, and the affairs of the consulate will be temporarily handled by Deputy Consul Tanaka. On the 19th, Tanaka visited Vice Minister Tang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to convey everything. (Special dispatch on the 19th)

Question in the British House of Commons

Problem of Chinese Railway Loans

(London) The arrears in the repayment of Chinese railway loans were mentioned again during today's meeting of the House of Commons. Conservative Member of Parliament Moreing said that the income of the Jinpu Railway is more abundant than before, but the clause in the contract that British engineers and traffic managers should be appointed has not yet been fulfilled, and the Chinese government should be urged to do so. Foreign Secretary Simon replied that the British Minister to China, Cadogan, has been constantly negotiating with the Chinese government on this matter recently, and will continue to make efforts to ensure that the Chinese government fulfills its promises. (Reuters dispatch on the 19th)

International Court Rules on

Case of Unpaid Interest on Russian-French Loans

(Nanjing) In the case of the loan from China to Russia and France in 1895, the interest was not paid when the contract was fully performed, which led to litigation in the International Court. Fufoulou Nan, of the International Commercial Bank, who represented China in the negotiations, wired the Chinese General Customs Service from Paris, deciding to pay 800,000 Swiss francs in compensation to resolve the case. The Inspector General of Customs has submitted the matter to the responsible officer for approval. (Special dispatch on the 19th)

Li Zongren's Representative Arrives in Beijing

(Nanjing) Li Zongren's representative, Liu Shouchu, arrived in Beijing on the 18th. He is scheduled to meet with President Wang in the coming days and present Li's personal letter. (19th Dispatch)

Pang Songzhou Corrects

His Report at the Ministry of Finance's Memorial Week

(Nanjing) Pang Songzhou, the Chief of Accounting at the Ministry of Finance, issued a correction on the 19th due to inaccurate reports of his presentation during the ministry's memorial week. According to Pang, what he reported that day included: (1) The method of allocating tax revenue and the process of allocating funds to remote and impoverished provinces after stamp tax tickets were sold on behalf of the post office; (2) The situation of planning the budget for the 24th year of the Republic, mentioning that the three major tax revenues from customs, salt, and consolidated taxes were slightly lower in July and August of this year due to the off-season and the impact of disasters, compared to the average monthly amount in the budget for the 23rd year of the Republic. It is still difficult to predict whether the total annual statistics will reach the budgeted amount. There was no mention of a decrease compared to the same period last year. (18th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The embassy in Belgium reported that more than 50 overseas Chinese have lost their jobs and are experiencing hardship. The Executive Yuan decided to remit 10,000 yuan to help the overseas Chinese return home. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Central Propaganda Department Explains Article 14 of the Publication Law

(Nanjing) The Guangxi Provincial Party Headquarters requested an explanation of Article 14 of the Publication Law. The Central Propaganda Department explained as follows: (1) If the facts are obvious and the evidence is conclusive, newspapers are not obligated to publish rebuttals; (2) If the text of a correction or rebuttal is complex and lengthy, it can be published in installments, or the requesting party can be consulted to shorten it; (3) Corrections of corrections must be published; (4) After a manuscript is published, the newspaper assumes full responsibility. Requests to disclose names should be kept confidential in good faith. The Central Propaganda Department has notified the Ministry of the Interior to implement these guidelines. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Military Council held its 83rd regular meeting at 10 a.m. on the 19th. More than 20 people attended, including Wan Fulin. Bao Yue chaired the meeting. Four routine cases were resolved, and four cases were reported. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Ji Hongchang's Estate Coveted by Others

(Beiping) After Ji Hongchang was executed, several of his former subordinates, known as the "Thirteen Taibaos," demanded that Ji's family divide Ji's estate equally. Their attitude was firm, and if their demand was not met, they would resort to drastic measures. Ji's family, due to their uncouth nature and difficulty in dealing with them, Ji's wife, Hu Hongxia, took her son and fled Tianjin, hiding in Beiping. As a result, no one came forward to handle Ji's funeral arrangements, and Ji's coffin remains at Changchun Temple. (19th Dispatch)

Miyun Faces Salt Shortage

(Beiping) Since the end of the war last year, Miyun's rural areas have been in a state of bankruptcy, with all industries declining. Recently, the Chengde puppet provincial government banned the import of blue salt, causing sales in areas such as Xiazhen and Baimaguan in Miyun to increase rapidly, three or four times more than the previous month. Salt merchants' stocks are running out, and new salt has not arrived, so Miyun County is facing the risk of a salt shortage. (19th Dispatch)

He has also ordered the security team to arrest and severely punish unruly elements if non-group organizations do not comply with the order to disband. (19th Dispatch)

In addition, there is a continuous stream of smuggled goods, mainly textiles, rayon, and sugar. Japanese goods account for a large proportion of the goods in various stores. Some even use steamships to transport private goods exclusively, making it extremely difficult to combat smuggling. He is deeply grateful to be going to Manchuria as the Commander of the Army and Ambassador to Manchukuo. Japan's policy towards Manchuria respects its independence and promotes its sound development. The fundamental policy is the complete integration of Japan and Manchukuo. The first method is to always respect the independence of "Manchukuo." If the Japanese people regard "Manchukuo" as a protectorate or colony, the prestige of "Manchukuo" will be undermined, which may lead to the division of Japan and Manchukuo. The second method is economic integration. Cooperation between Japan and Manchukuo in economic industries is essential. The development of products in "Manchukuo" requires huge capital. The combination of Japan and Manchukuo requires capital, and developing its industries, increasing revenue, and improving the economic level will strengthen the foundations of both countries. Resignation of Yugoslav Foreign Minister

Leads to Cabinet Collapse

Disagreement over League of Nations Compromise Plan

Military Faction Seizes Opportunity to Seize Power

Belgrade: Disagreements among cabinet members regarding the League of Nations' compromise plan for resolving the Yugoslavia-Hungary dispute have led to the collapse of the Yugoslav cabinet today. This crisis is the most important turning point in Yugoslav history, as the cultural, military, and political issues of Yugoslavia will be resolved at this time.

The crisis began when some cabinet members refused to approve the League of Nations' resolution, resolving the Marseilles case, causing great anger to Foreign Minister Yevtich. According to some cabinet members, the League of Nations' resolution was not enough to compensate for the assassination of the Yugoslav monarch and did not guarantee the cessation of future terrorist acts. They questioned Foreign Minister Yevtich about the purpose of accepting this compromise. During the cabinet meeting on Monday, Foreign Minister Yevtich briefly outlined his views, and some cabinet members severely criticized him, making him feel embarrassed. His attempt to appease them only led to even more criticism. By the time the cabinet reconvened today, a stalemate had been reached, and the entire cabinet resigned. The resignation declaration was issued at 8 p.m. tonight, after a day of acrimonious debate. Army generals, who have been waiting for a long time, have now stepped forward, seeing that the government has finally given them an opportunity, and demanded to seize power in this time of national crisis. It remains doubtful whether the military is willing to accept the League of Nations' compromise plan. If they are unwilling, the turbulent situation in the Balkans is just beginning. (18th National Press Dispatch)

Belgrade: Before submitting his resignation, Yugoslav Foreign Minister Yevtich had a heated dispute with Prime Minister Uzunovic in the cabinet meeting. At the height of the dispute, Yevtich stormed out. Agricultural Minister Korosec, who agreed with Yevtich's attitude in the cabinet, also submitted his resignation. As a result, the cabinet crisis became unstoppable and had to submit a general resignation. It is understood that the dispute arose from internal problems. It is understood that Prime Minister Uzunovic has other political enemies in the cabinet besides Yevtich and Korosec. Therefore, Uzunovic is unlikely to be appointed to the new cabinet. Furthermore, the Regent has already summoned the leaders of the Croatian and Slovenian parties, which were previously dissolved, to negotiate the formation of a new cabinet. This is indeed a surprising move. According to sources from Yun Tong, the Regent intends to form a cabinet of national unity, with the current Chief of the Army, Zivkovic, as the Prime Minister. Zivkovic has already begun seeking the opinions of opposition party leaders. (18th National Press Dispatch)

Yevtich Ordered to Form a Coalition Cabinet

Yugoslav Capital: This morning, Prince Regent Paul continued to seek the opinions of various political parties in an attempt to resolve the cabinet crisis. It is generally believed that former Foreign Minister Yevtich was ordered to form a new cabinet after meeting with the Regent this morning. Some even said that the Regent gave Yevtich "unlimited delegation" to form a broad-based coalition cabinet, inviting leaders of some opposition parties who were banned after January 6, 1929 (when the late King Alexander I implemented a dictatorial system) to participate in the new cabinet. Judging from the Regent's meetings with the leaders of these parties yesterday and this morning, there is generally a reason for this. (19th Havas Dispatch)

British House of Lords Passes India Constitutional Report

Labour Party Members Abstain

(London) The House of Lords debated the government's proposals on India for four days. Mussolini's Great Construction

Reclaims Marshland into Province

Arduous Work Still Requires Ten Years to Complete

Emperors and Popes of Past Dynasties Failed to Achieve

Rome: Italy now has a new province called Littoria, which was originally marshland. People began to dredge it in 312 BC. After repeated efforts by emperors and popes of past dynasties, it was never completed. This marshland often emitted poisonous gases, posing a hazard to travelers. Italian Premier Mussolini decided to complete what his predecessors had failed to achieve through his efforts. However, the work has been going on for a long time, and the canal project has not yet been completed. Today, the Italian Premier held a ceremony to establish the new province, saying that this work will require another ten years to be completed. In order to maintain this great work and prevent it from being interrupted, Italy must have a larger military force. Those who heard this applauded continuously. The Italian Premier's speech was broadcast throughout the country, and anyone with a radio at home could hear it. (18th Reuters Dispatch)

Commentary

On the French-Russian Military Alliance Heng

Yesterday, a London dispatch stated: The French-Russian military agreement was formally established on the 22nd of last month. Its main points are (1)

that the two countries will cooperate in military technology and manufacturing, and (2) that they will plan for joint

response with Germany and Japan as hypothetical enemies. Recalling a Paris dispatch on the 24th of last month, Radical Socialist Party member Ah Xiangbo claimed that a defensive alliance had been established between France and Russia. In the event of any trouble between Germany and France, Soviet Russia would definitely support France. For a time, the international atmosphere was extremely turbulent. The French government

immediately denied this. The inside story was really unknown at the time. It was unexpected that after a month, the British newspaper spoke with certainty, indicating that most people already believed that there must be considerable truth to it. Now the French again have an indication of denial. However, we, from the facts to ponder, then it seems that France really has the possibility of concluding such an alliance with Russia. (1) Because France has a historical fear of Germany. Therefore, no matter how superior its own military preparedness is, or how numerous its sympathizers are, it always feels that its own security is still not complete. Since the French lack confidence in their own strength psychologically, they naturally consider it wise to form alliances with powerful countries. (2) Since the French and Russians initiated the Eastern European Pact, Poland has never expressed support because it does not want Russian troops to pass through. Germany wants to exchange for military equality and is unwilling to accept unconditionally. Britain is only guiding all parties from the sidelines and does not take any responsibility for whether it succeeds or not. Therefore, the Eastern European Pact has been brewing for more than half a year, but has not achieved anything. Given this situation, it is impossible to promote the realization of the Eastern European Pact without further action by France and Russia. (3) The cooperation between France and Italy has been actively progressing recently, but there are many difficulties between the two sides. It is still uncertain whether they will be able to reach a completely harmonious state. (4) If the French-Russian military agreement is successful, even if the Eastern European Pact cannot be realized, it will in fact have the effect of the pact to a certain extent. Looking at the content of this military agreement, it only emphasizes the exchange of military personnel and the mutual supply of munitions, and does not mention that Soviet Russia will send troops to jointly attack Germany. This point seems to be a step for France to plan to contact Poland, because in this way, Poland can avoid the danger of Russian troops passing through. Therefore, after this agreement is concluded, Poland may be able to change its attitude towards France. With these

factors, it can be seen that the rumors of the conclusion of this agreement between France and Russia may not be accidental.

If this agreement is indeed concluded, its impact will certainly not be limited to Europe. According to Article 4 of the agreement, if Soviet Russia is attacked by Japan, France will immediately supply munitions to Russia, etc. From this, it can be seen that if something happens to Japan and Russia, France will inevitably be involved. Since France does not maintain neutrality but supplies munitions to Soviet Russia, Japan has sufficient reason to provoke conflicts in French Annam. In the past, foreign telegrams stated that France was afraid of offending

Japan, so it was unwilling to conclude an agreement with Russia that would involve the Far East war. The meaning of France's continued denial of the French-Russian military alliance may lie in this.

US Senate Opposes the Opening of the Nicaragua Canal

Because it benefits coastal states and harms inland states

Senator Clark, a member of the Senate Interoceanic Canal Committee, expressed his opposition to opening the Nicaragua Canal today. Clark declared that this plan would greatly help the development of US coastal states and harm inland states. It is reported that the proposal to open the Nicaragua Canal was advocated by Mr. Vincent, Chairman of the House Naval Affairs Committee this week, who said that it would be submitted to Congress. (National Telegram, 18th)

Japanese Privy Council Meeting

Decision to Abandon the Naval Treaty

Breaking the Balance of Power in the Pacific

Ambition to Dominate the Far East is Clearly Exposed

The US is Temporarily Unwilling to Express its Opinion

(Tokyo) This morning, the Privy Council held a full meeting in the presence of the Emperor and unanimously supported the Japanese government's decision to abolish the Washington Naval Treaty. It is reported that the formal note of abolition of the treaty will be sent to the US State Department after the Christmas holiday. (Reuters, 19th)

(Tokyo) The advisory proposal to abolish the Washington Treaty was passed by the Privy Council today. Therefore, the government immediately requested the issuance of the proposal and attached it to tomorrow's cabinet meeting. After the decision, Prime Minister Okada immediately requested approval. On the morning of the 22nd, Foreign Minister Hirota telegraphed Ambassador Saito in the United States, instructing him to notify the US government. Therefore, Ambassador Saito will observe the situation and then personally deliver the notice to the US government. If it can proceed smoothly, it can be implemented on the 22nd. At the latest, all procedures can be completed on the 27th after Christmas. (Telecommunications, 19th)

(Tokyo) The government will send the notice of abolition of the Washington Treaty to Ambassador Saito in the United States, and also intends to briefly explain the main purpose of the abolition. However, it is necessary to observe the changes after the adjournment of the London talks before changing the plan. However, it is decided to explain the reasons for the abolition notice to the public. The original text has been discussed by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Navy, and the text is more than 1,200 words long. (Telecommunications, 19th)

(Washington) State Department officials are unwilling to comment on the Japanese Privy Council's formal approval of the abolition of the 1923 Washington Naval Treaty. It is understood that no statement will be issued until a formal notice of abolition is received through diplomatic channels here. However, spokespersons close to the government unofficially declared that Japan's actions would be regarded as disrupting the political and naval treaty system that maintains security in the Pacific. The abolition of the treaty can also be regarded as the prelude to the arms race among the countries concerned in the Pacific. According to the opinions of observers here, if Japan obtains naval equality with Britain and the United States after abolishing the Washington Treaty, Japan will be sufficient to dominate the Far East. The power of most Westerners now will be eliminated, and the historical rights obtained by European and American countries in Asia, such as the open door policy of China, will also be harmed. (National Telegram, 19th)

Naval Negotiations to Adjourn

Japan's Last Efforts

Requesting a Provision for the Date of Reopening

(London) Although the US representative has received instructions from Washington to temporarily suspend the tripartite naval talks according to the British plan, the Japanese representative is still making final efforts to decide on the date of resumption of discussions. According to the British plan, the procedures for this issue will be determined by Britain. US representative Davis told Japanese representative Matsudaira today that the US attitude has not changed, believing that Japan's abolition of the Washington Treaty has suspended the negotiations. A request to resume talks can only be made when new events are discussed. Matsudaira replied that Japan insists on inserting a specific date for the resumption of talks. (Reuters, 19th)

The United States Changes its Neutrality Principles

The Intention is to Subdue Japan

One Party is Sufficient to Strengthen the League of Nations

One Party Pleases Britain to Obtain Support

Not Contrary to Major Diplomatic Strategies

(Washington) The State Department is preparing to submit a proposal to President Roosevelt, advocating a complete revision of the US neutrality principle and the establishment of a new principle. This matter was seen in yesterday's telegram. Secretary of State Hull confirmed it, but also said that the outside world's statement that the United States will abandon its traditional principle of freedom of the seas is "completely speculative." According to some sources, if other countries go to war in the future, the US President may announce that US ships that venture to sail in war zones, and US arms merchants who trade with warring countries, will be responsible for the dangers they may encounter, and the US government will no longer provide assistance. This policy can enable the United States to cooperate with the League of Nations on the one hand, and satisfy Britain and France on the other. If the League of Nations imposes a blockade on a certain country, it does not need to worry about the United States. As for Britain and France, they have always said that the United States' complete conservatism and neutrality is sufficient to hinder the efforts of the League of Nations. Now that the United States has changed its principles, the situation has changed. The Washington government's change of principles is related to the naval talks. Because Japan's demands on the navy are unyielding, the United States believes that if it wants to subdue Japan, it will not succeed without the assistance of Britain or Soviet Russia. The change of neutrality principles is to please Britain and make it support the United States. (Havas Telegram, 18th)

(Washington) If the most powerful country in the world tries to evade responsibility and remains isolated, it will be impossible for the country and the world to avoid the most serious consequences. President Roosevelt recently advocated amending the neutrality principle, and what he told the American people is this. President Roosevelt is now preparing to make the United States have a consistent theory in resolving various international relations. The principles on which it is based are as follows:

(1) The United States will remain neutral in armed conflicts.

(2) On the one hand, it will avoid forming alliances with foreign countries, and on the other hand, it will cooperate with a series of powers and international leagues, and within the limits permitted by the US Constitution, jointly seek to maintain peace.

(3) Prevent US arms manufacturers from obtaining excessive profits from war, so as to prohibit US manufacturers from colluding with foreign industries.

(4) When the United States encounters attacks from other countries, it must stand undefeated. From now on, prepare a national mobilization plan to enable the US Navy to build the largest fleet permitted by the Washington Treaty, build the most modern navy, and open the Nicaragua Canal to connect

the Atlantic and Pacific Oceans and complement the Panama Canal.

Since taking office, President Roosevelt has declared that he will not interfere in the internal affairs of Latin American countries, but will strengthen good neighborliness with Latin American countries, and has restored US-Russian diplomatic relations, all of which have been successful. Although there are disputes over naval issues between the United States and Japan in the current London talks, the relations between the two countries are still satisfactory. Therefore, regarding the war debt issue, although President Roosevelt has always maintained the rights that the United States should have, he has still tried his best to avoid aggravating the disputes. The new diplomatic theory announced by Roosevelt this time is compatible with the major diplomatic principles of the United States in the past, such as Pan-Americanism, the Monroe Doctrine, and the Open Door Policy in China, and does not run counter to them. Not only that, but the US government and people have recently become more convinced that Anglo-American understanding is the main condition for world peace. If the principle of freedom of the seas is modified, it will inevitably make Anglo-American understanding closer. In addition, the State Department's plan to President Roosevelt to modify the neutrality principle stipulates that the President is allowed to issue orders to prohibit the export of munitions, prohibit loans to warring countries, and prohibit the passage of ships carrying goods and munitions to warring countries from berthing in US ports. (Havas Telegram, 18th)

(Washington) Charles Warren, who served as Attorney General in the government of the late President Wilson from

1914 to 1917, recently published an article in a diplomatic magazine on the issue of the new neutrality principle being considered by the State Department, and proposed a principle that in future wars, especially in naval wars between countries such as Britain and Japan, if the United States wants to maintain the principle of freedom of the seas, it will inevitably be dragged into the vortex. Therefore, he advocated that the US President has the right to abandon or maintain all rights concerning neutral countries. Whether these neutrality rights are violated and whether the violation can be used as a reason for declaring war, and submitting it to Congress for deliberation, should also be at the discretion of the President. Until after the outbreak of the war, only the President can enjoy the following rights:

(1) Monitor all radio stations in the country and prohibit foreign diplomats from sending coded messages. (2) Prohibit the sale of weapons to warring countries. (3) Prohibit warships of warring countries carrying weapons or gun emplacements from entering the country. (4) Order all ships of warring countries to leave the United States. (5) Prohibit US ships from supplying ships of warring countries. (6) Prohibit US citizens from subscribing to public bonds of warring countries. (7) Prohibit foreign representatives from recruiting their own nationals in the United States to form volunteer teams.

Duris, an advisor to Norman Davis, the chief US naval representative, expressed his approval of the above claims, saying that US policy must be brave and have considerable flexibility, so as to become a real force to maintain peace, and can take effect before the war starts. (Havas Telegram, 19th)

Franco-German Rapprochement

A Powerful Guarantee for European Peace

Laval's Recent Diplomatic Statements

Urging Germany to Join the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact

French Chamber of Deputies Passes Special Military Expenditure of 800 Million Francs

Today, during the Senate's discussion of the foreign affairs budget, Foreign Minister Laval delivered an important declaration. He began by stating that the resolution of the Saar issue and the South Hungarian disputes by the League of Nations was of utmost importance. The calmness of both South Hungary and the proactive mediation of other countries to quell the unrest were both commendable. Regarding Franco-Italian relations, he stated that negotiations were underway, aiming to harmonize the opinions of both countries not only on matters of particular concern to them but also on general policies. Mr. Laval praised Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's spirit of conciliation, stating that the compromise that France and Italy intended to reach would absolutely not harm the interests of the Little Entente countries. The Foreign Minister then spoke of the negotiations for the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact, saying that France made this proposal only after reaching complete agreement with Soviet Russia. "The collaboration between France and Russia is being conducted openly, and its purpose is to benefit the public." Mr. Laval mentioned Germany, stating that France would never take any action that would make Germans suspect France of pursuing any policy that would trap Germany in isolation. "France will soon negotiate with Germany again, urging Germany to conduct negotiations with France and other countries on equal terms, and urging it to join the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact, with all the guarantees granted to other signatory countries also being available to Germany." Mr. Laval concluded by saying, "The rapprochement between France and Germany within the international arena is indeed an effective guarantee of peace." (Havas Dispatch, 18th)

Mr. Laval also disclosed the full text of the Franco-Russian draft of the treaty promoting the Eastern European Locarno Pact. Before Mr. Laval spoke, Navy Minister Pietri stated in the Senate that naval construction must be accelerated and insisted that the naval construction budget for 1935 must be 1.2 billion francs, compared to 900 million francs in 1934. Mr. Pietri also said that France had always regarded the Washington Naval Treaty as a "temporary necessity," so France refused to jointly abolish the treaty with Japan to avoid offending Britain and disrupting peace in Europe. (National Telegram, 18th)

(Paris) Today, the Chamber of Deputies passed a supplementary budget of 800 million francs with a vote of 460 to 130 to fund the bill to reform France's war supplies. The Socialist Party had proposed an amendment advocating that armaments be manufactured by the state and that the arms trade be controlled by the state starting from January 1st next year. Prime Minister Flandin treated this amendment as a matter of confidence, and the Chamber of Deputies ultimately struck down the Socialist Party's amendment with a vote of 388 to 199. The Radical Socialist Party requested that the issue be debated in January next year, which the government accepted. (Reuters Dispatch, 18th)

(Paris) According to the Army Ministry's budget proposal, the special national defense expenditure of 800 million francs is allocated as follows: (1) Artillery and other military equipment: 615,500,000 francs; (2) Engineering Corps: 48,000,000 francs; (3) Military Supplies: 35,000,000 francs; (4) Health Affairs: 15,000,000 francs; (5) Ammunition: 80,000,000 francs; (6) Railways: 6,500,000 francs.

When the proposal was discussed by the Chamber of Deputies this morning, Prime Minister Flandin spoke repeatedly, explaining the needs of national defense. As a result, the proposal was passed with a vote of 460 to 130. Besides the orthodox socialists voting against it as usual, the communists on the far left actually voted in favor, which is an unprecedented situation in the history of world parliaments and is worthy of attention. During the discussion in the morning, former Aviation Minister Cot demanded that the arms manufacturing industry be nationalized, saying, "We are sincerely willing to serve on the battlefield, but on one condition, that we know that war is not a source of wealth for a few." Prime Minister Flandin replied that he very much wished for the nationalization of arms manufacturing, but France's experience in the European War was enough to prove that if France had relied solely on its own arsenals during the European War, it would have long lacked defensive weapons and been defeated by the enemy. France demanded that countries that love peace establish an international convention on the sale of arms and supervise it. "As for France, it has already strived to reduce its armaments to the lowest limit. If it is still unavoidable to strive to plan national defense anew, then the blame does not lie with France. There is now a great power that is increasing the number of arms manufacturing plants, with monthly manufacturing expenses between 350 million and 600 million francs. Is this something we can do? In short, for the sake of France's security, we must first seek it from ourselves and then seek it from others." When the discussion continued in the afternoon, the newly elected Socialist Party member Berane expressed his views, acknowledging the danger of Germany's rearmament. He said that the new Socialist Party would vote in favor of the special national defense expenditure bill and would use this bill as a reason to oppose increasing the term of military service (referring to increasing the term of military service from eighteen months to two years). Army Minister General Maurin rose to speak, requesting the Chamber of Deputies to pass the special expenditure bill with a spirit of sacrifice, saying that France's military equipment had become obsolete and should be renewed. He also said, "France's border defenses cannot be like China's Great Wall, thousands of miles of continuous interconnection. There must be places where defenses are not set up, which must be plugged." General Maurin also promised to establish a team of technicians to engage in technical work on border defenses. (Havas Dispatch, 18th)

Disarmament Conference Enters a State of Sleep

Committee Work Still in Progress

(Geneva) The Disarmament Conference has entered a state of sleep since the Presidium met once on November 20th, but its affiliated agencies are still continuing to work. This can be proved by the conference's National Defense Expenditure Committee. The committee has now completed drafting the convention on national defense expenditure and has prepared a report advocating that (1) signatory countries must have the obligation to mutually notify all expenditures related to national defense; (2) stipulating the methods of publicizing and supervising the national defense budget, with three times for publicizing and supervising: (A) when the budget is passed; (B) if there is an increase or decrease in expenditure, it will be carried out nine or fifteen months after the event; (C) after being reviewed by the domestic high-level agency (this refers to the payment order and final account being reviewed by the audit agency). Experts believe that if this kind of national defense expenditure convention can be implemented, then military expenditure can be publicized, and the number of troops and weapons will also be publicized accordingly. There will be a close link between the two. The report is planned to be submitted to the Disarmament Conference within January next year. (Havas Dispatch, 18th)

Paraguay Accepts the Suggestion

(Geneva) The recent efforts of the League of Nations to resolve the Chaco dispute between Bolivia and Paraguay have failed. The League of Nations will consider it in the coming days. According to the suggestion put forward by the League of Nations, the two warring countries should convene a ceasefire conference in the capital of Argentina, with Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Peru, and the United States acting as arbitrators in the conference. If a ceasefire cannot be announced within two months, then it should be appealed to the Permanent Court of The Hague. If the war is stopped, then a military commission should be organized by representatives of the United States and South American countries to assist in demarcating a demilitarized zone of one hundred kilometers wide. Paraguayan Army Launches a Large-Scale Offensive Against Bolivian Troops with 80,000 Soldiers

The Sound of Artillery Never Ceases Day and Night

La Paz The Paraguayan army launched a large-scale offensive against the Bolivian defense line today with a force of 80,000 soldiers, intending to occupy Villa Montes, the gateway to the Chaco oil region. The Paraguayan army does not expect to obtain it easily, so it will open the most intense scene of the Chaco War in more than two years. At present, the sound of heavy artillery never ceases day and night, and it can be vaguely heard dozens of miles away. The most intense war is centered on the Fort Boquerón. The Bolivian communique stated that the Bolivian army has concentrated all its strength in the most dangerous location, which is extremely difficult to shake. If the Paraguayan army occupies Villa Montes, it can drive straight in and attack the Bolivian mainland. (National Telegram, 18th)

America's Attitude Towards the Situation in the Pacific

Implementing the Movement of Fleets Between the Two Oceans

The London Naval Reduction Preparatory Conference is intermittent. Britain has repeatedly put forward trial plans, but they do not conform to the facts. The claims of Britain, the United States, and Japan differ, so it has been shelved. The United States has recently been busy with elections, busy with the "New Deal," and busy with domestic issues such as unemployment relief. It seems that it is not very active in the maritime situation in the Pacific 丨丨future naval competition丨丨 and has no specific claims. However, it knows that Japan's abolition of the naval treaty will be realized. Verbal reconciliation may not be effective, so it is also engaged in practical military work, wanting to support its claims with its actual strength.

The strength includes its natural various mineral deposits, the production capacity of the current industrial sectors, and all its means of transportation, including the sea, land, and air forces. It is not easy to review them one by one. Fundamentally speaking, the strength of the United States is of course the most powerful country in the world. However, since 1929, it has been hit by the economic panic, and the signboard of permanent prosperity is unreliable. Now, it may be said that its strength has been slightly depleted, and far-reaching ambitions may be difficult to achieve for a while. It is important to solve domestic problems first. However, we know that the United States has fully developed into a modern industrial country. Even its agriculture has progressed to mechanized management, so it cannot maintain the status quo by relying solely on the domestic market. Moreover, maintaining the status quo is not a fundamental solution. Then, it must work hard to develop overseas markets like Britain and find economic outlets from abroad. After the European War, the United States has already become a huge financial capital country, emphasizing financial investment overseas and de-emphasizing the consumption of goods. However, recently (since Germany stopped paying reparations in 1931), European countries have successively defaulted on debts, and so has South America. Britain may not pay the debts due at the end of this year, so foreign investment is not very reliable. Therefore, it cannot help but try to stabilize the sales market again to promote the vitality of the industry.

The countries along the Pacific coast are all excellent consumption markets. Whether it is cotton, steel, machinery, etc., they are all promising in the future. However, the relationship there is quite complicated, and the competition is also very fierce. Moreover, the United States does not have a special sphere of commercial influence in the Far East. In the current era of state-controlled economic development, competition is not very convenient. Militarily, even if there are the Philippines and Guam, the locations are too far apart. The Philippines will be independent in ten years, and Guam is a small place, so how can it have the ability to support it? Therefore, the United States must rely heavily on the navy to give it full ability to protect maritime navigation. The US Navy is indeed second only to Britain, and cruisers and submarines are also inferior to Japan. Only battleships can barely cope, and they are separated in the Americas, between the two oceans. Once an incident occurs, it is very troublesome to concentrate troops.

Fortunately, the Panama Canal has been opened, and the connection between the two oceans can be done without much effort. This spring, the Pacific Fleet crossed the canal eastward, taking 48 hours. This time, more than 130 warships and 100,000 soldiers came westward, but it only took 41 hours and 40 minutes to cross the canal. Its speed and agility are truly increasingly improving. From now on, the Atlantic Fleet and the Pacific Fleet can be more easily integrated into a group, no longer subject to geographical restrictions, going east and west freely. In the future, it will combine the Atlantic and Pacific fleets together, this year on this side, next year on that side, constantly moving to train its own soldiers. At the same time, it also slightly injects into the nearby residents. The fleet's supplies and the expenses of the soldiers' families are also a large consumption.

Why does the US government not hesitate to spend more on the movement of warships, ordering the two-ocean fleets to sail once a year? This is the US Navy's recent response. Because of its auxiliary ships, there were those built well. Separating and stationing the two fleets will make it difficult to handle in the event of an incident. It will be very disadvantageous if it falls into a passive position. Therefore, it must break through this type of natural restriction, making full use of its military strength, so that its imaginary enemies have scruples, and at the same time, it also takes care of the Philippines and its overseas markets in the Far East, wanting its maritime routes to have full protection, and hinting at its strong strength. As for using this to subsidize the economic turnover of the garrison area, that is a relatively small matter. (November 25th in Washington)

Japanese and Korean Ruffians Ordered to Withdraw from the War Zone

Ruffians Engage in Selling Drugs and Gambling

Our Side's Requests Lead to Japanese Crackdown

Beijing Correspondence: Japanese and Korean ruffians in the "war zone" usually specialize in selling drugs and setting up gambling dens. After our side repeatedly requested the Japanese side to crack down on them, the Japanese side recently ordered the ruffians to withdraw within a time limit. According to people from Tangshan, when the Japanese and Korean ruffians in the city received the order from the Japanese Military Police Department on the 14th, they immediately convened a general meeting to discuss measures and decided to comply with the order to withdraw. Therefore, in the past few days, the Japanese and Koreans have been preparing everything and auctioning off furniture to serve as travel expenses in order to leave. The number of Japanese and Korean residents on the streets of Tangshan should be reduced starting from New Year's Day next year. According to the Zunhua County Government's report to the relevant parties here this morning (18th), the illegal shops of the Japanese and Korean ruffians in the county were also notified by the Japanese military police yesterday to close immediately and pack up to return to Japan. Those who fail to comply within the time limit will be forcibly expelled. The Japanese and Korean ruffians in the county are also preparing to leave the area. The reporter specifically inquired with the relevant parties about the truth, and it was said that both China and Japan believe that it is necessary to crack down on the trouble caused by the Japanese and Korean ruffians in the "war zone." After repeated discussions, the Japanese side agreed to deal with them separately. The recent order for the Japanese and Korean ruffians in Tangshan, Zunhua, and other places to withdraw is the beginning of the implementation of the crackdown. If the crackdown on the Japanese and Korean ruffians in the counties in the war zone continues step by step, then the security in the "war zone" can be expected to gradually become consolidated, and the benefits to the friendly feelings between the people of China and Japan will also be not small. (18th)

Ferguson's Collection of Antiques Donated to China in Full

Temporarily Stored in the Antiquities Exhibition Hall

Exhibition to Begin on New Year's Day

Beijing Correspondence: American scholar Dr. Ferguson has stayed in China for more than forty years. He usually collects curios worth about 3 million yuan, totaling more than 1,000 items. Recently, due to old age and in memory of his founding of Jinling University, he specially donated all of his beloved antiques to the university. However, because the university does not yet have suitable buildings for display, it was decided to first store them in the Antiquities Exhibition Hall and display them in a special room in the Wenhua Hall. A draft agreement was signed by the three parties and notarized by lawyer Lin Xinggui on the 12th of this month, and the formalities for the contract were completed. The moving began yesterday (14th), and the ticketed exhibition will begin after New Year's Day next year. Dr. Ferguson's move is deeply admired by all parties, regardless of whether they know him or not. Those who went to Ferguson's residence to pay their respects have been especially numerous in recent days. The names of the antiques, the original text of the draft agreement, the representative's remarks, and the display plan are detailed below.

Names of the Treasures The antiques donated by the doctor are of many types. Here is a selection of the most precious and rare treasures: (1) Bronzes: Zhou Ke Ding, Zhou Bronze Drum, Human-Headed Whirligig, Twenty-Sixth Year Edict, Circular Ruler, Bronze Pen (2) Jades: Scepter, Bi, Cong, Dance Axe, (3) Pottery: Ancient Pottery Urn, Bowl, Colored Writing on Large Jar. In addition, there is a tiled house from the tomb of Li Xian of Wei and a tiled coffin from the tomb of Liu Yiming of the Song Dynasty. (4) Porcelain: Various kiln wares from the Yin and Shang Dynasties to the Qianlong Dynasty. (5) Paintings: Among the hand scrolls are Qi Han's Peach Ear Picture (with inscriptions by Su Dongpo and Wang Jinqing of the Song Dynasty), Li Longmian's Self-Portrait of Five Hundred Arhats of the Song Dynasty, Qian Xuan's Zhu Geliang's Southern Campaign Picture, Shen Zhou's Various Plum Blossom Pictures of the Ming Dynasty, Qiu Ying's Biographies of Women of the Ming Dynasty. Among the calligraphy scrolls are Jing Hao's Mountain Villa Picture, Zhu Mayuan's Plum Blossom Seeking Picture, Five Kinds of Landscapes by the Eight Masters of Jinling of the Qing Dynasty. Among the figure paintings are the Image of the Supreme Being, Yang Bangji's Man Riding Picture of the Jin Dynasty, and Lang Shining's Western Ladies Picture of the Qing Dynasty. Among the flower and bird paintings are Peony and Peacock Picture by a Song Dynasty person, and Wild Goose Picture. (6) Books: Wang Youjun's Jialu Tie of the Jin Dynasty, Sixteen Letters of Song Sages, Song Tuoben Renzhi Tie (with inscriptions by Weng Fanggang). In addition, there are more than 1,000 kinds of rubbings.

Draft Agreement for Donation and Entrustment The original text of the draft agreement for donation and entrustment: Ferguson, an American citizen, currently residing in Beijing (hereinafter referred to as Party A, which refers to the donor to Party B, the recipient, and the entruster to Party C, the entrusted party), as one party.

Chen Yuguang, President of Capital Jinling University (hereinafter referred to as Party B, which includes the successors of the university), as the other party, and Qian Tong, Chairman of the Antiquities Exhibition Hall of the Ministry of Interior (hereinafter referred to as Party C, which includes its successors under public law), as the third party.

Party A came to China in his early years and participated in the founding of Nanjing Huiwen College, which has now been expanded into Capital Jinling University. Afterwards, he continued to engage in education and cultural undertakings in China for more than 40 years. Because of his deep love for Chinese cultural relics, he successively invested in the collection of bronzes, jades, porcelain, pottery, inkstones, inks, calligraphy, paintings, steles, gold stones, and other rubbings, accumulating to more than 1,000 pieces. Now that he is old, based on his friendly feelings towards China, he intends to make public to China what he has obtained from China, and because he served Party B the earliest, he is willing to donate them to Party B for preservation. Moreover, because Party B is willing to accept the aforementioned donation, but because there is no building for storage, it is not easy to break, and it has not yet been received, and at the same time, Party C is willing to first accept the entrustment and allocate the Wenhua Hall for display for public exhibition. Once the buildings of Jinling University are completed, they will be transferred again. After submitting to the Ministry of Interior the instructions for the first two numbers, etc., based on the above-mentioned reasons, the three parties negotiated the draft agreement as follows. Article 1: Party A hereby donates the aforementioned bronzes, etc., the types and details of which are detailed in the list of items attached to this agreement, to Party B for permanent preservation, but does not assume any defects in the donated items, and hopes that Party B will bear the following burdens and conditions when receiving compensation: (1) To complete a strong building in the Chinese style within a considerable period of time to store and display the donated items. The cost of this building shall not be less than silver dollars 40,000; (2) The donated items shall be allowed to be exhibited to people outside the school on time, and shall not be transferred or disposed of without the approval of the antiquities preservation and supervision authority; (3) In the event that Party B is dissolved, the donated items shall belong to nearby academic organizations engaged in the same purpose. Party B hereby accepts Party A's donation in accordance with the burdens and conditions attached to the preceding paragraph. Article 2: Party C promises to Party A to allocate the Wenhua Hall as the place for displaying the items before Party B actually receives the donated items. After this draft agreement is submitted to the Ministry of Interior for approval, it will immediately go to Party A's residence to check and collect the entrusted items according to the attached list of items, without charging Party A for transportation and storage expenses or remuneration. Party C shall be responsible for the entrusted items, except for force majeure such as natural disasters, for good safekeeping. All income from admission tickets will be used for the needs of layout and routine safekeeping. Once Party B sends a letter informing that the buildings have been completed, Party C shall jointly with Party B negotiate the transfer deadline, submit it to the Ministry for approval, and then send personnel to properly install the items for transportation to Beijing. All expenses shall be borne by Party B. The transfer shall also be supervised by the Ministry to show solemnity. Article 3: The procedures for terminating the entrustment, transferring possession, etc., shall be negotiated separately by Parties B and C at that time. This draft agreement and the list of items are written in four copies. When Party C submits it to the Ministry of Interior for approval, the Ministry seal shall be affixed to the agreement and sent to Party C for distribution to the parties for signature. When the signature is completed, it shall become a formal contract and take effect. Of the above four formal agreements, one copy shall be submitted by Party C to the Ministry of Interior for record, and Parties B and C shall each hold one copy. The remaining copy shall be delivered to Party A for Party A to copy and keep for future reference by his heirs. The original shall be sent by Party A to the Embassy of the United States for record, so as to be trustworthy. Attached List of Items. December 12th, 23rd year of the Republic of China. Party A, Donor and Entruster, American citizen Ferguson, Party B, Recipient, President of Jinling University Chen Yuguang, Party C, Entrusted Party, Director of the Antiquities Exhibition Hall of the Ministry of Interior Qian Tong, Drafter of the Agreement, Lin Xinggui, a student of Party A.

Representative's Remarks According to the representative of Dr. Ferguson's remarks to the reporter, Dr. Ferguson has lived in China for 47 years, came to China in 1887, and founded Jinling University in Nanjing in 1888. Later, he served as the President of Nanyang University in Shanghai and as an advisor to the President's Office. Afterwards, he moved north to reside. The doctor highly respects Chinese culture and is interested in historical relics. For decades, he has spent money collecting them, totaling thousands of items. Recently, due to his advanced age, based on his enthusiasm for returning to China what he obtained from China, he decided to donate all the antiques to Jinling University for preservation and as a permanent memorial to the founding of the school. Currently, because the school does not have suitable buildings, they are temporarily displayed in the Antiquities Exhibition Hall. A draft agreement has been established by the three parties to ensure compliance with the agreement.

Display Plan The Antiquities Exhibition Hall received an order from the Ministry of Interior to follow the instructions for the registration and display of Ferguson's antiquities. Yesterday (14th), people were sent to Ferguson's residence to move the items. According to Fu Yiwen, Section Chief of the Second Section of the Hall, "The Hall originally designated the Wenhua Hall as the exhibition room for Ferguson's antiquities, but the hall has not been completely cleaned up due to the short period of time. It must be cleaned up before the display can begin. However, it has been scheduled to open after New Year's Day next year. At that time, the ticket price will be determined after it is submitted to the Ministry." (15th)

Northwest Inspection Record Special reporter of this newspaper, Geng Ya

Following Finance Minister Kong's Solemn Denial of Rumors

Market Turmoil Subsides

Gold Standard Bonds Return to Normal

High Foreign Exchange Rates Are a Common Year-End Phenomenon

According to Huadong News Agency, recent rumors in Shanghai about the government implementing inflation led to extreme volatility in the trading market. After Finance Minister Kong solemnly declared these rumors untrue to Huadong News Agency reporters the night before last, yesterday, all trading gradually stabilized. The reporter has learned the following details about yesterday's situation:

Recovery Process

Following the sudden rise of rumors in recent days, various transactions experienced drastic fluctuations, causing widespread panic. This was especially true for gold standard bonds. After Huadong News Agency reporters learned from Finance Minister Kong that the rumors were untrue, yesterday, gold standard bonds and securities gradually stabilized. Yesterday, the central government's listed standard for rising gold standard bonds was 1005.80. The highest price in the gold market did not exceed 1000 yuan, and the lowest was only 993.7 yuan, a difference of only 5 yuan and 3 jiao. Market transactions favored a small number of small long positions, with fewer short positions. The government bond market was also relatively stable, with a difference of less than one yuan. Yarn, cloth, flour, and other commodities have also gradually returned to normal, with a difference of only two or three jiao for flowers and only seven or eight jiao for yarn and cloth. Although there were slight fluctuations in the afternoon, they were very few.

Cause of the Rumors

According to Huadong News Agency reporters, who have been investigating the cause of these rumors in the market, banking circles, industrial circles, and semi-official circles for several days, the rumors were deliberately spread by speculators. It was said that during the Fifth Plenary Session of the Central Committee, a certain committee member proposed implementing inflation. Fortunately, the timing was not ripe, and the proposal was not brought up. The rumor-mongers seized the opportunity to create rumors benefiting either long or short positions, causing widespread panic in the market and plunging the market into a precarious situation. According to financial giants, the United States is the world's gold superpower, and even their implementation of inflation has not been very effective. It is absolutely impossible for our country to do so at this time, and the government will definitely not implement it. There is no need for people in the market to worry needlessly and give outsiders a chance to manipulate the market, they said.

Foreign Exchange Rates Rise Again

Yesterday, the foreign exchange rate was 3 jiao and 5 fen in both the morning and afternoon, 5 fen higher than the day before. The "劃頭" rate was also higher, at 3 jiao and 8 fen. On the surface, it seems to be gradually tightening again, but in reality, this kind of situation is an extremely common phenomenon in the ten-odd days leading up to the Chinese New Year. According to people in the money industry, speaking to Huadong News Agency reporters, although money is slightly tighter this year than last year, it cannot be said to be unusually tight. During the two New Year festivals of the Zhilu War in 1924 and the founding of the National Government in Nanjing in 1927, the highest peak of 7 jiao per tael was once reached, they said.

Salt Revenue Audit Office Repays

Crisp Loan Principal

Totaling £96,049 British Pounds

According to a Guofa News Agency report from Shanghai on the 19th, Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi announced today that the Director of the Salt Revenue Audit Office has remitted £96,049 to London for the repayment of the principal and interest of the 1928 term of the 1912 Crisp Loan. According to the 1929 Salt Revenue Debt Reorganization Plan, all overdue interest on the Crisp Loan was cleared in 1930, and the Anglo-French Loan of 1908 was also cleared in mid-October of this year. The overdue principal of the Crisp Loan can now be repaid. The payment made this time for the 1928 term is the initial step in clearing the arrears.

Newly Appointed Chairman Huang of Zhejiang Province

No Definite Date to Assume Office in Hangzhou

Secretary-General Huang Huabiao to Depart First Yesterday

Huang Shaoxiong, the newly appointed Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, took a train to Nanjing from Shanghai on the evening of the 9th to attend the Fifth Plenary Session of the Central Committee and to request policy instructions from the central government. Having completed his public duties, he returned to Shanghai by train from Nanjing the day before yesterday. According to Huang's aides, speaking to Xin Xin News Agency reporters yesterday, Huang has appointed the newly appointed Secretary-General of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, Huang Huabiao, to handle the takeover matters of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, departing for Hangzhou on the 19th. As of yesterday, the date of Huang's own departure to Zhejiang to take office had not been decided, but it is expected to be within the next few days, they said.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company General Manager Liu Hongsheng Returned to Shanghai Yesterday

"Haiheng" Imported from Qingdao Yesterday

"Haizhen" Expected to Arrive on the 26th

According to Central News Agency, the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Haiheng" ship, which recently made its maiden voyage to Haizhou and Qingdao, returned to Shanghai yesterday morning and is scheduled to sail to Shantou, Guangzhou, and other ports at noon on the 21st. The "Haili" ship is currently being painted and will be received soon, with a maiden voyage scheduled. The "Haizhen" ship, currently sailing to China, is expected to arrive in Shanghai on the 26th. The details are as follows:

"Haiheng" Returns to Shanghai The state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Haiheng" ship, which was shipped to Shanghai at the end of last month and officially received, sailed to Haizhou and Qingdao the day before yesterday for its maiden voyage. General Manager Liu Hongsheng, Business Section Chief He Molin, and others from the company traveled with the ship, inviting local gentry and merchants to visit the new ship and taking the opportunity to inspect the newly completed Lianyungang Port in Haizhou. They completed their tasks the day before yesterday and returned south. The ship entered the Songkou port at about 8:00 yesterday morning and docked at the Jinliyuan Wharf at 9:30, carrying a large amount of intermodal cargo from both locations.

He's Remarks According to Section Chief He, who returned to Shanghai yesterday morning, the "Haiheng" ship made a very good impression on the local people in Haizhou and Qingdao. The newly completed Lianyungang Port is currently only large enough to berth one ship. However, with the implementation of water-land intermodal transport in the area, the cargo volume is very high, so the dock is still insufficient. The staff of the local bureau are working day and night and are very busy. He also said that the company's new ships are entirely for use on the South China shipping routes. "Haili" is being painted As for the "Haili" ship, which arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday, it is currently being painted by the Jiangnan Shipyard. It will be completed and received soon, with a scheduled departure. The "Haizhen" ship, which is currently en route, is expected to arrive around the 26th of this month, according to the Shanghai representative office of the British shipbuilding company, Malcolm & Co. At that time, all four sister ships ordered and built in England will be completely taken over by the company and will operate between the two major ports of Shanghai and Guangzhou, they said.
