International Trade Bureau

Convenes Exporters' Meeting Yesterday

To Coordinate the Promotion of Trade in Southeast Asia

The International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, in view of the global economic panic, the continuous decline of export trade, and the increasing trade deficit, convened a meeting of Southeast Asian export traders at the bureau's conference room at 2:00 p.m. yesterday to seek opinions in order to find a way to save foreign trade. Those in attendance included Guo Zhenjia (Da Xing Hang), Xie Yian (Nanqiao Hang), Zhao Guide, Qian Zhongfu (Zha Hua Company), Kong Zuan (Jun Chang Hua Hang), Zhao Zibin, Zheng Houdong (Jinhai Trading Company), Wu Hankang (Baolai Hang), Chen Zizhang, Shi Defang (Yihua), Shi Yulin (Cheng Chang Silk Store), and Liu Shimu, who is familiar with Southeast Asian market conditions, totaling more than a dozen people. Deputy Director Guo Chengbo presided over the meeting and Ji Zejin recorded the minutes. The chairman reported the purpose of the meeting and then began soliciting opinions from the participating representatives on trade with Southeast Asia and future plans. The topics discussed at the time included freight, export tariffs, export bills of exchange, bank export standards, and commercial ethics. Experts Liu Shimu and Qian Zhongfu contributed their opinions. Because the content was complex, it was necessary to coordinate with the Ministries of Communications and Finance before convening another meeting at a scheduled time to decide how to handle the matter.

China Factory Federation

Planning to Hold a Shanghai South National Exhibition

Filed with the City Party Department and Social Affairs Bureau Yesterday

The China National Products Manufacturers Federation, in order to complete the national product promotion for the Women's National Products Year and in accordance with the provisions of its charter, has launched the Shanghai South District National Products Exhibition to give the residents of the Shanghai South District a deep impression and to seek effective promotion of national products. Preparations have already begun, and registration has begun. It is reported that the federation filed a document with the City Party Department and Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, which stated: "Submitting for review and filing the matter of holding the Shanghai South National Products Exhibition to benefit the promotion of national products. Advocating national products places the greatest emphasis on promotion. The National Products Exhibition is the most effective promotional method for advocating national products and resisting foreign goods. In the face of increasing foreign aggression and national crisis, advocating national products and cultivating the national foundation are particularly important tasks at present. In view of this, this association is holding the Shanghai South National Products Exhibition to give the public a deep impression and to promote national products effectively. The site has been determined to be the vacant lot at the entrance of Hengxing Lane on Lima Road in the 16th Pupu, and it is scheduled to open on New Year's Day next year. In addition to submitting to the City Social Affairs Bureau (Shanghai Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party) for filing, we have prepared a document to submit to your association (bureau) for review. We respectfully request that you approve the filing to facilitate the promotion of national products, which is in the public interest."

Overseas Chinese Expelled from Japan

The Twenty-First Group Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Chen Zhilan and Three Others

Returned Home Aboard the "Shanghai Maru"

Overseas Chinese in Japan have been unreasonably expelled by the Japanese authorities. More than two hundred people have returned to China one after another. At 3:00 p.m. yesterday, another twenty-first group of expelled overseas Chinese, including Chen Zhilan, Xu Baohan, Guo Zuoqing, and Ye Hongmin, arrived in Shanghai aboard the "Shanghai Maru." After landing, they stayed at the Lao Gongxin Inn in the Nanshi district. Hearing the news, reporters from the Shiye News Agency immediately went to inquire. According to Xu Baohan, "Chen Zhilan and I were in business in Kobe. Guo Zuoqing and Ye Hongmin were working in Nagoya. We were all law-abiding and did not break the law. Unexpectedly, we were expelled by the Japanese authorities and forced to return home, which is extremely hateful. When we were escorted onto the ship, the Chinese Consulate made representations, but the Japanese authorities turned a deaf ear and acted arbitrarily," he said.

Commander of the Japanese Training Fleet

And Three Princes Arrive in Shanghai

The Fleet Docked at the Huishan Wharf Yesterday Afternoon. Japanese Residents Held a Grand Welcome.

According to Huadong News Agency, Commander Nakamura of the Japanese Extraordinary Training Fleet and three Japanese princes arrived in Shanghai from Qingdao at around 12:00 p.m. yesterday. Japanese dignitaries went to welcome them. They are scheduled to return to Japan on the 22nd. Huadong News Agency reporters have made a special note of the following:

Arriving in Shanghai Yesterday Rear Admiral Nakamura, Commander of the Japanese Training Fleet, led 300 naval academy graduates aboard the "Asama" and "Yakumo" ships from Sasebo at the beginning of the month to conduct practical training at sea. After arriving in Qingdao, they stayed for several months, visited scenic spots, and paid visits to Mayor Shen and naval authorities of various countries. They left Qingdao for Shanghai at 3:00 p.m. on the 17th and arrived at the port at around 12:00 p.m. yesterday, docking at the Huishan Wharf. Japanese Welcome Consul General Ishishe, the Japanese military and administrative officer stationed in Shanghai, representatives from the embassy, ​​Ashino, Arino, Yokokawa, Commander Hyakutake of the Third Fleet, Chief of Staff Kondo, Commander Araki of the Marine Corps, Police Chief Hanazato, as well as the chairman of the Resident Association, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, and other overseas residents, all went to the ship to welcome them.

The Princes on Duty On this visit to Shanghai by the two ships, three princes are on duty in the navy: Prince Asaka Yasuhiko, a gunnery officer on the "Yakumo" ship, and Prince Fushimi Hiroyoshi, an ensign candidate on the "Asama" ship. The three princes also arrived in Shanghai with the fleet for practical training. Therefore, in addition to welcoming Commander Nakamura, the Japanese residents and military and administrative officers expressed their welcome and respect to the three princes.

Banquet Sequence The Japanese Naval Academy Cadets in Shanghai, in recognition of the three princes' service in the navy and their visit to Shanghai, have specifically scheduled a grand welcome reception at the Japanese Club in Hongkou at 6:30 p.m. today (the 20th). In addition, the Training Fleet Executive Committee is also scheduled to hold a banquet for the three princes and naval officers at the same location at noon on the 21st. As for the three princes and Commander Nakamura, they are scheduled to return to Japan on the 22nd.

All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association Requests Tax-Exempt Passports for Foreign Rice

Standing Committee Meeting Yesterday Decides to Purchase Grain for Distribution

The All-Zhejiang Drought Relief Association of the Jiaxu Year (1934) held a standing committee meeting yesterday. Those present included Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Shenzhi, Wang Rutang (representing Wu Tianfang), Qian Junren, Xu Xinliu, Chu Huiseng, Hu Fengxiang, Zhuang Yuqing, Yu Zhongxian, Xu Jilun, Lu Zhinan, Xu Qianlin, Fan Zhenchu, Wu Zhihao, Zhang Weiru, Zhou Shouliang, He Dekui, Wang Yiting, and more than twenty others. Chu Huiseng presided over the meeting. Reports were made on telegrams from various places requesting relief. The following were then discussed: (1) Qian Junren, the director of the relief in the third district, reported on the situation in Shangyu, Xinchang, and Shengxian counties. The disaster situation in the Kunlian districts of the three counties is very serious, but due to the county boundaries, they are not within the scope of the investigation and relief. It was decided to allocate 2,000 yuan each to Lihai in Shaoxing and Liangnong in Yuyao, and to ask Director Qian to separately solicit donations from charity groups and fellow villagers, to be combined for relief. (2) A motion to add Ju Nianqu as a standing committee member of the association was passed. (3) The Jiaxing County Government requested an additional allocation of relief grain. It was decided to reply by letter, stating that it would be discussed further when donations were sufficient. (4) A letter was sent to the Zhejiang Relief Association inquiring about which of the remaining three counties under its responsibility for relief would be given priority and requesting a prompt reply. It was decided to proceed accordingly. (5) The drought relief associations of various provinces allocated theater tickets as cash to the association. The association has registered the receipts. When selling the tickets, many were returned due to expiration. It was decided that those returned before the expiration date would be compensated by the members of the association, and those returned after the expiration date could not be accepted. The ticket sellers were asked to forgive the payment. (6) It was resolved to transfer Wukang, Deqing, and Yuhang to the drought relief associations of various provinces for investigation and relief.

The association believes that Wenling, Huangyan, and Pingyang in Zhejiang have had abundant rice harvests this year. Therefore, it plans to send personnel to purchase 40,000 dan of rice and 20,000 bags of flour in the near future, specifically for the victims in Jiaxing, Tongxiang, and Fengde counties. It also plans to purchase 100,000 dan of foreign rice from Siam and Saigon. Yesterday, the association sent a letter to the National Government Relief Committee requesting the issuance of passports, stating: "To whom it may concern, the drought in Zhejiang Province this year is widespread and affects a large population, requiring a huge amount of relief grain. The rice produced in Zhejiang Province has always relied on commercial transportation from other provinces such as Xichang, Xiang, and Gan to make up for the shortfall. Now, all regions have been hit by drought, and the sources have been exhausted. The prospect of people's food is a matter of great concern. After repeated discussions, this association has decided to send personnel to purchase 100,000 dan of relief grain from Siam, Saigon, and other places, to be shipped to Shanghai in batches and then transported to the counties most severely affected by the disaster in the interior, for winter and spring relief. However, in order to save relief funds, we earnestly request that you forward this to the Ministry of Finance to check the regulations on tax exemption for disaster relief items, and approve the Jianghai Customs to exempt the import tax on this relief grain, in order to benefit the poor and heavy the government with disaster relief. We have prepared two copies of the application form for tax-exempt passports, a total of ten sheets, and respectfully send them to your committee for review and forwarding to the Ministry of Finance for issuance of tax-exempt passports for the procurement of large quantities of relief rice. We earnestly request your review and approval for implementation, which is a truly kind act."

Promoting the Use of Domestic Fir Timber

Telegraph from the Fir Timber Industry Association of the Upper Min River: "To the Executive Committee of the Central Party Department in Nanjing, Military Affairs Commission Chairman Chiang, National Government Chairman Lin, Executive Yuan President Wang, Finance Minister Kong, and Fujian Provincial Party Affairs Commissioner Chen, We humbly report that Fujian Province has always been a major producer of fir timber, which is not only related to the livelihood of the entire province but also a source of national wealth. Five years ago, the annual output reached more than 40,000, with a value of more than 10 million. In recent years, the Communist bandits have been wreaking havoc in northern Fujian, coupled with the apportionment of military supplies and the imposition of exorbitant taxes, and local ruffians extorting money, the costs along the way exceed more than twice the cost. As a result, the timber industry has suffered a disastrous defeat, and timber workers have gone bankrupt. The annual output has decreased year by year, to less than 10,000. More than 20 counties in the upper reaches of the Min River, and millions of workers, all depend on the timber industry for their livelihood. Now, they are facing starvation, and they are bound to take risks. The main reason is the illegal collection of fees. It is understood that the 19th Route Army in Fujian, in order to provide sufficient supplies for the Liu and Lu units, created a temporary defense subsidy fee at Shuikou, collecting 45 yuan per large timber raft. The original plan was to abolish it after six months, but it has been two years now and there is still no clear order for exemption. In addition, He Gonggan, the former Director of Finance of the pseudo-People's Government, established a bureau in Zhuqi and collected a timber raft business tax on the way, which is no different from a transit tax, levying it at more than 60 per thousand. This practice is still followed today, coupled with the extortion of local ruffians everywhere, causing great pain and suffering. Timber workers have repeatedly complained to the association, with tears in their eyes. Although the organizing office of this association has repeatedly sent telegrams to the Nanchang headquarters, appealing to order the Fujian Provincial Government to abolish the temporary defense subsidy fee and rectify the timber raft business tax, we have been informed that the Fujian Provincial Government has been instructed to investigate and handle the matter. At the same time, we have appealed to the Fujian Provincial Government, presenting the same situation, and strictly prohibiting the extortion of local ruffians along the way, all of which have been filed for several months, but have not been implemented. If this continues, the future of the timber industry will be ruined. Considering that the government's policy is to first alleviate the suffering of the people, and that the central government has issued a clear order to exempt exorbitant taxes, and the provinces have successively implemented it, Fujian Province, which has suffered from the Red disaster for a long time, should be given extra care and treated equally. We dare to telegraphically appeal for your sympathy, to reduce the burden of merchants, and request that you submit this to the Fifth Plenary Session of the Central Committee, and immediately order the Fujian Provincial Government to abolish the temporary defense subsidy fee at Shuikou, rectify the timber raft business tax, and order the garrison along the way to strictly protect the timber industry, and issue a ban on illegal collection along the way, in order to relieve the suffering and maintain the timber industry. In addition to sending representatives to Nanjing to petition, we respectfully submit this to you. We are filled with apprehension and await your orders. The Fir Timber Industry Association of the Upper Min River kowtows."

Ministry of Finance Approves Chamber of Commerce's

Method for Exchanging Old Stamps

To Wait for Each Provincial Bureau to Submit and Verify the Total Number Before Devising a Proper Plan

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce received a reply telegram from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "Your telegram has been received and acknowledged. The stamp tax revenue has been stipulated to be used for offsetting the abolition of land tax surcharges and exorbitant taxes in each province, city, and county, in accordance with the resolutions of the National Finance Conference, which is of utmost importance to alleviate the suffering of the people. Therefore, the exchange of old stamps for new stamps must be based on the principle of not causing a major impact on future tax revenue. After the chambers of commerce in each province and city complete the registration, how should they be exchanged in stages will depend on the number of registrations in each province and city. Since it is impossible to predict in advance, the method of exchange must be determined separately after the stamp and alcohol tax bureaus in each province submit the total number of registrations for review by the ministry. Previously, the Taicang County Chamber of Commerce directly telegraphed the ministry, and a reply was sent informing them to proceed with registration within the prescribed time limit and not to harbor doubts and wait and see. It is commendable that the chamber of commerce has been actively handling the registration matters. After completion, they should promptly compile a list together with the original application and send it to the Jiangsu Stamp and Alcohol Tax Bureau for verification and forwarding. This is the approval."

To Inspect South China This Morning

The Position of Consul General is Temporarily Filled by Mr. Davis

Mr. Cunningham, the American Consul General stationed in Shanghai, who also leads the consular corps in Shanghai, is planning to make a tour of South China as the year is drawing to a close. Norwegian Consul Talks

Investigation into the Harvard Incident

Yesterday, Only Over a Hundred Bags of Sunken Rice Were Salvaged

According to the Kwok Man News Agency, after the Tung Tak steamer, represented by the Ta Fa Shipping Company, collided with the Norwegian Harvard steamer, represented by the Mei Shun Company, both parties are currently investigating the matter of responsibility, while the insurance companies are carrying out salvage work. The news obtained yesterday is recorded as follows:

Tung Tak Enters Dock The Tung Tak steamer, yesterday morning at ten o'clock, was towed from the 43rd pontoon in Pudong into the old dock of the Yih Sung Shipbuilding Plant in Pudong, opposite Dongjiadu, and the accumulated water was drained in the afternoon. It is scheduled for nine o'clock this morning to invite the Shanghai Navigation Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, and the China United Marine Insurance Company, to jointly send marine surveyors to inspect the vessel at the old British dock in Pudong.

Continued Salvage of Sunken Rice The Harvard steamer was loaded with over ten thousand bags of Siamese rice. Apart from the four hundred-odd bags salvaged the day before yesterday, yesterday, the three insurance companies, Yangtze, Jardine, and New Zealand, hired laborers, wearing rubber suits, to continue diving and salvaging. However, because many of the rice bags were broken due to the expansion of the rice grains, and they were difficult to carry out, only over a hundred bags were salvaged yesterday. There are still ten thousand bags of rice in the ship. If salvage work is not stepped up, there is no hope for the Harvard steamer to resurface.

Consul's Talk Yesterday, according to Mr. Gilder, Vice Consul of the Norwegian Consulate in Shanghai, who was interviewed by a reporter from the Kwok Man News Agency, this Consulate summoned the parties involved to the Consulate at three o'clock in the afternoon yesterday (the 18th) and held a hearing. In Norwegian legal terminology, its nature can be translated as a maritime investigation tribunal. Apart from the ship owner, pilot, chief mate, second mate, and chief engineer of the Harvard steamer, who were all present at the hearing, the personnel of the Tung Tak steamer did not comply with the summons and were not present. At the hearing, the speaker served as the presiding judge, and the two ship owners, Nuvan and Persson, served as jurors. The purpose of this investigation is to make a detailed and factual legal record of the details of the incident, for use as a basis for future negotiations, arbitration, or compensation. As for how to arbitrate in the future, this Consulate has neither received any request from any party nor has any preconceived notions as to who is responsible. As for the purpose of holding this investigation tribunal yesterday (i.e., the day before yesterday), it was to submit the hearing records to the Norwegian government.

Customs Notice Mr. Guthe, Acting Harbour Master of the Jianghai Customs, issued a notice yesterday stating that the Norwegian Harvard steamer is currently sunk near Lujiazui in Section 4 of this port, its position is about two hundred feet downstream from the Lujiazui port police stationed ship, and the stern extends into the navigable waterway for about two hundred feet. The masts, chimneys, and upper parts of the ship can be seen regardless of the tide. All navigating vessels should navigate on the Puxi side of the sunken ship and should reduce their speed so that they can stop at any time. Furthermore, salvage operations are currently underway. All vessels should also pay attention to the fact that the sunken ship's signal will be hung on the foremast and stern flagpoles. During the day, it will be a green flag, and at night, it will be one green light and one white light, strung vertically. All shipping merchants are hereby notified. Acting Harbour Master Guthe.

Settlement of Compensation for the Deceased Crew of the Mount Tai Steamer Resolved Yesterday

Senior Employees Receive One Year's Salary According to Maritime Law

Lower-Level Crew Members Receive a One-Time Compensation of Five Hundred Yuan Each

According to the New Voice News Agency, the Mount Tai steamer of the Hua Merchants San Pei Steamboat Company, which sailed from Qingdao to Shanghai on the 26th of last month, had an accident en route. The families of all the deceased crew members repeatedly requested the company to resolve the aftermath. In addition to the unpaid wages, which had accumulated to more than three months for all crew members, which the company's manager, Mr. Yu Qiaqing, paid in advance, the compensation funds were delayed for more than ten days and had not been resolved. Yesterday, representatives from the Chinese Marine Engineers Association and various groups in this port personally negotiated with Mr. Yu, the manager of the company. It was agreed on the spot that the chief engineers and first and second assistant engineers of the engine department would each receive one year's salary in accordance with the provisions of maritime law. As for the lower-level crew members, because their full-year salary was not much, they would each receive five hundred yuan. The families all accepted. In addition, there was the issue of cultivating the crew members' children. Manager Yu also agreed to find suitable schools on their behalf and bear the costs, so that they could find employment and resolve their livelihood, in order to comfort the deceased.

Memorial for Mr. Yao Zirang's Passing

People from All Walks of Life Initiate a Public Memorial Service

Two O'Clock in the Afternoon on the 26th

Since Mr. Yao Zirang passed away last winter, people from all walks of life have deeply mourned him. The 26th of this month is the anniversary of Mr. Yao's death. Therefore, elders and celebrities such as Tang Wenzhi, Wang Qingmu, Wang Zhen, Liu Yazi, Huang Qinglan, Zhang Jia'ao, Chen Taoyi, Shen Weixian, Qin Xitian, Huang Yanpei, and Shen Enfu have initiated a public memorial service at the Guandi Temple inside the West Gate of Shanghai at two o'clock in the afternoon on that day. All memorial items will be collected by the temple on their behalf. Those who wish to participate in the memorial service can go there at that time.

A Plea for Relief

The Ren Ji Road Sino-Foreign Relief Association received reports from various drought-stricken counties in Jiangsu Province yesterday, recorded as follows: (1) A letter from Father Chen of the Catholic Church in Lishui County states that Lishui County is surrounded by Huangshan mountains, which stretch across the entire county. The residents cultivate the land at the foot of the mountains, and the land is barren, resulting in very poor harvests. This summer, there was a three-month drought, with no rain at all. The fields cracked. Initially, the farmers pawned their belongings and hired laborers to irrigate the land, but then the ponds and reservoirs dried up, and they had to watch the crops wither. The autumn harvest was only one-tenth or one-twentieth of normal. There was no harvest to speak of. It is not uncommon to see parents carrying their children into the city seeking food. There are also those who cultivate over a hundred acres of land but have no grain to cook and are waiting to die. In short, the entire Lishui County, except for a few embanked fields in the Shijiu Lake area in the south, which yielded seventy to eighty percent of the normal harvest, is in extreme distress. Now that it is deep winter, there is no rice to eat and no clothes to keep warm. The various tragic scenes are unbearable to witness. If relief is not provided urgently, the number of poor people who will die of starvation, freeze to death, or become displaced will be countless. (2) A letter from Father Li of the Catholic Church in Jurong County states that Jurong is surrounded by mountains on all sides, and the area is vast and the terrain is very high. The harvests have been poor for many years, and the people have long been unable to make a living. This summer, the drought was devastating, lasting for three months. The high and low-lying fields were dry and cracked, and there was no autumn harvest. Even the by-products were poor. People's livelihoods were on the verge of collapse. As a result, there was eating from door to door, fleeing from famine, robbery, begging, and selling daughters. Such tragic and cruel acts are unprecedented in decades. Currently, farmers are filling their stomachs with Guanyin powder, chaff powder, and sweet potatoes. In addition, it is winter, and the weather is cold with no clothes to keep warm. If no measures are taken to provide relief, they will inevitably die in ditches. Please send personnel to investigate and provide relief. (3) A letter from the Drought Relief Committee of Jintan County states that our county is a poor area in Jiangsu Province. Even in years of good harvest, the people can hardly make ends meet. This summer, the rainfall was exhausted, and the farmland was turned into red soil. The farmers have no surplus savings and no seeds to harvest, so they eat grass roots and sell their children to barely survive. The severity of the disaster is the worst among the disaster-stricken counties in Jiangsu Province. Now that it is deep winter, there are no fewer than tens of thousands of people waiting to be fed. If relief is not provided in time, it will inevitably harm society and is of great concern. Therefore, we earnestly request the allocation of funds for relief. It is heard that the association is facing difficulties in raising funds due to the widespread drought and the difficulty in donations, and the cotton power is limited. It is hoped that all sectors will lend a helping hand to alleviate this crisis.

Jiading Fellow-Villagers Association Provides Assistance

An Helpless Woman is Threatened

A Letter is Sent to the Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association to Investigate the Truth

According to Li Guisu, a female fellow-villager of the Jiading Sojourners Association in Shanghai, she has been subjected to grievances and threats and is seeking assistance. A letter was sent to the Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association to inquire about the truth. The letter reads: "We are writing to inform you that yesterday, Li Zhangshi and her daughter Li Guisu, fellow villagers, came to the association and claimed that Guisu lost her parents at an early age. Zhangshi worked as a domestic helper in Shanghai. When Guisu was seventeen years old, she also came to Shanghai and worked as a female worker in the Japanese-owned Neiwai Spinning Mill on Robison Road in October of the 20th year of the Republic of China. Later, someone arranged for her to marry Wang Yaoqing, a Ningbo native who worked as a foreman in the same factory. Guisu's mother, because she only had one daughter and hoped to be together in life and death and burial in the future, instructed the matchmaker to explain to Wang Yaoqing, Wang readily agreed, so the marriage was arranged in November of that year, receiving a betrothal gift of one hundred yuan. Then, the January 28th incident of Japanese aggression in Zhabei occurred, and Shanghai went on strike. Guisu had no work to do. In this chaotic situation, the mother and daughter were helpless, so the matchmaker came and Wang Yaoqing lived together, so that there could be discussions if anything happened. At that time, Guisu's mother thought that since the marriage had been arranged, although the wedding ceremony had not been held, they would always be husband and wife in the future, so she agreed. During the intense warfare, Wang Yaoqing had no work to do and stayed at home all day. Without any suspicion, Guisu was seduced. Although they were not married, they had already shared a dream. At that time, they lived in Lane 2, Shankang Lane, Robison Road. Then, Guisu became pregnant, and Wang Yaoqing moved his family to No. 277, Yaozu Lane, Dongyouheng Road, Hongkou. In the first half of the 21st year, although the war had ended, the pregnant woman could not work. Wang Yaoqing was also unemployed, so Wang did not seek a way to make a living, but stayed at home drinking and gambling all day. Since the family had no savings, they had no choice but to pawn their belongings to survive. There are pawn tickets to prove it. Then, Guisu gave birth to a son, who died after five months. Wang Yaoqing then asked Guisu to be a wet nurse, receiving a child to raise, and using the wet nursing fee to cover the family's expenses. In reason, Wang Yaoqing relied on Guisu for his livelihood, and they should have been able to live in peace. However, Wang did not seek a living outside, but instead looked for trouble at home, scolding her when he had no wine, and even beating and abusing her. The situation was unbearable. When Wang Yaoqing was engaged, his betrothal money of one hundred yuan was originally borrowed. When he was unemployed, it had not been paid off. Guisu helped to repay it. There is a debt collector named Xiangfu Niang who can testify. Living like this, there was no joy in life. In desperation, Guisu went out to work as a wet nurse. Unexpectedly, Wang Yaoqing falsely accused Guisu of running away. Guisu avoided his fierce flames and sneaked back to her mother's home. Wang actually fabricated words to accuse her, falsely accusing Guisu of being familiar with someone, and falsely reported to the Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association, and together they arrested Guisu and took her to the Xizang Hotel on Xizang Road, forcing her to pay ninety yuan to break off the relationship. Guisu's mother and daughter were originally lonely and helpless. Such a large sum of money was impossible to obtain. Li's mother reported to the police station, stating Guisu's suffering from threats and abuse. The police station inquired about the situation and released her, and ordered Wang Yaoqing not to engage in such private detention in the future. Who knows that the Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association does not ask right from wrong, but listens to one side of the story, and even Yu Qiaqing comes forward to negotiate with the Public Works Department, which is so powerful. For this reason, they came to request assistance. They also brought a copy of the Ningbo Daily on December 12 and a copy of the Shanghai Local Court Prosecutor's Office's decision not to prosecute the defendants Wang Zhangshi, Wang Yaoqing, etc. The Standing Committee of our association decided that fellow villagers who have been wronged should be helped. If what Li Guisu said is true, then Wang Yaoqing's actions are inhumane. However, our association deeply feels that the content of this matter must be very complicated, and we cannot fully believe Li Guisu's mother and daughter's words. Your association has been handling this matter for a long time, and you must have a detailed investigation. Therefore, we have appointed Standing Committee Member Weng Guoxun to contact you and ask for details in person: (1) What is the relationship between Li Guisu and Wang Yaoqing? What was the previous dispute? (2) What is the truth about Li Guisu's claim that your association sent personnel to accompany Shi Yaoqing to arrest Li Guisu and take her to the Xizang Hotel on Xizang Road, forcing her to pay ninety yuan to break off the relationship? We hope that you can tell us. Sincerely, the Jiading Sojourners Association in Shanghai.

The Eighth Large-Scale Muslim Delegation

Going to Mecca to Pray

The Entire Delegation Consists of 126 People

Departing Today on a British Steamer

In recent years, Muslim believers in our country have gone to Mecca to perform the prayer ceremony. There have been seven previous delegations, and this year is the eighth. Its scale is larger than previous delegations, and the number of believers going to Mecca reaches more than 120. The China Travel Service has been preparing for days and has been very busy. The details will be described below, departing at 3:00 PM today:

Crowded Delegation This year, the Muslim believers participating in the prayer ceremony at the holy land of Mecca include a total of 110 male members such as Hei Ji, Ma Wenhui, Ma Tingxiang, Na Yanjin, Ye Weixin, Bai Chengyu, Fa Zhi, Hai Changqing, Zhan Deshan, Jin Sanli, Yang Shengchun, Mao Lantian, and Wang Jinde, 14 female believers including Ma Hongda's sister-in-law and two sisters, and two children, who are the sons of Mr. Ma Xiaodeng. Therefore, the total is 126 people. Ninety percent of the delegation members are from Gansu, and the rest are from Suiyuan, Chang'an, and Henan, with only about a dozen people. All of them arrived yesterday and gathered at the mosque, where Mr. Jin Ziyun took care of everything.

Completed Procedures The large number of believers this time is rare in previous delegations. Each believer going to Mecca must apply for a passport and undergo a medical examination. The procedures are very complicated. This matter was fully entrusted to Mr. Deng of the China Travel Service by Mr. Jin Ziyun of the local mosque to handle. Until yesterday, all passports had been obtained, and the medical examination of each believer was also conducted by four male and female doctors sent by the seaport inspection office, who examined each believer and issued a doctor's examination certificate, which was issued by the travel agency to each person for safekeeping.

Agreed on a Special Steamer Previously, Mr. Deng of the travel agency negotiated with the British Blue Funnel Line for the use of the Pyrrhus, a large ship of over 7,000 tons. All passenger seats were provided for the Muslim prayer delegation, and a direct voyage from Shanghai to Jeddah was requested. As a result of the negotiation, the Blue Funnel Line agreed to a direct voyage from the Pyrrhus to Jeddah, taking the route through Singapore. The Nanyang branch of the travel agency will take care of them when the ship arrives in Singapore. A telegram has been sent from Shanghai. After the believers disembark in Jeddah, they will travel by land to the holy land of Mecca. During this section, each person must ride a camel. It takes about five weeks from Shanghai to Mecca.

Travel Arrangements Of the entire delegation of 126 people, none of them know English, and most of the crew members of the Pyrrhus are British, and very few know Chinese. In order to facilitate the daily life of the delegation members and contact en route, the travel agency specially negotiated with the Blue Funnel Line to temporarily hire translator Mr. Ma Cunliang to serve as the interpreter for each believer and travel with the ship. The ship is specially equipped with Muslim food, mainly lamb. Each person will receive five taels of lamb every four days, and other foods will be provided intermittently, such as rice and noodles. A halal chef is specially hired in the kitchen to prepare dishes for each person. This time, the total cost of the round-trip travel expenses, including camel fees, etc., for all the believers going to Mecca for the pilgrimage is approximately 120,000 yuan.

Departing Today Yesterday afternoon, the China Travel Service notified each believer to send their luggage to the ship first. The Pyrrhus is docked at the Blue Funnel Wharf in Pudong. All the believers will gather at the New Customs Wharf at 10:30 AM today and take a small steam boat specially sent by the Blue Funnel Line to the big ship. At 3:00 PM, it will depart from Shanghai and go to Wusong, then to Hong Kong, and then to Singapore, before going to Jeddah, which will take approximately 35 days at sea.

The Cai Yangqi Case Opens for the Eleventh Time

Lang Zuyin Continues to Defy Summons

Yesterday's Hearing Endorsed with "Await Scheduled Hearing"

Lang Zuyin, a Chinese detective from the Old Zhabei Police Station, arrested Cai Yangqi, a Chongming worker at the Longshun Gongdi freight company on Fujian Road Bridge South, during the spring in connection with a theft case at the company. Subsequently, the First Special District Court, after reviewing the case, found no evidence of Cai's involvement in banditry and ordered his release. After Cai returned home, his wife, Fan, seeing her husband injured and vomiting blood, filed a lawsuit with the First Special Court against Lang Zuyin and Bao Defu, the owner of the freight company, for assaulting her husband. This case has been ongoing for half a year, with the court holding eleven hearings. However, Lang Zuyin has consistently refused to accept the court's summons, citing orders from his superiors, and has failed to appear in court, making it impossible to begin the trial. Although the First Special Court petitioned the Ministry of Justice to forward the matter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the foreign legations concerned, requesting the Municipal Council to order Lang to surrender to allow the court to proceed according to law, these negotiations have yielded little result. Therefore, yesterday afternoon, when the case was scheduled for another hearing, Lang Zuyin still defied the summons and failed to appear. The presiding judge, Liu Yugui, endorsed the case with "Await Scheduled Hearing," indicating that there is no set date for the trial to begin.

Details of the Lianxing Customs Patrol Ship Capturing Pirates

Eleven Pirates and Twenty-Six Hostages

Sent to the Bureau for Interrogation Together at 2 PM Yesterday

Pirate activity has been erratic in the waters outside the Songkou port in recent years. Although customs patrol ships have been patrolling the area, there are many pirate gangs, and as one is suppressed, another rises. Incidents of looting ships and extorting ransoms continue to occur. On the afternoon of the 17th, the customs patrol ship Lianxing discovered a large sand barge that had been looted in the waters off Sheshan. After opening fire, they captured eleven pirates and rescued twenty-six hostages. Details of the pirate gang's origins and the capture are recorded below:

Pirate Life: The pirate gang consisted of twenty-eight members, equipped with handguns and Mauser pistols. They have no fixed address and have been roaming the seas for several years. They started by seizing a ship as their base, sharing food and lodging. They then continued to rob or kidnap people to make a living. They frequently switch ships, making it extremely difficult for patrol ships to track them down. Recently, they have expanded from one ship to two (both Ningbo-style sand barges). Except when they encounter patrol ships, which they quickly try to evade, they frequently roam the sea, causing much harm to merchant ships.

Kidnapping for Ransom: On the 11th of this month (Lunar November 5th), the pirates kidnapped Tong Zhubao and Zhou Pinsheng, two Ningbo natives who were catching crabs near Shenjiamen, and forced them to do hard labor, demanding a ransom of 200 yuan for each. On the 11th, they kidnapped Gong Bie, a shuangdang fisherman, in the same area. A "shuangdang" fisherman refers to two fishermen who jointly pull a net. The profit from each catch is managed by the trading company. The pirates only kidnapped one fisherman from each pair, instructing the other to report to the trading company and arrange for a ransom. They kidnapped eleven Ningbo people in total, including Liu Chuxing, Shi Shengxia, Tang Shunfa, Xin Linsheng, Xin Ali, Dong Linsheng, Yu Dingsong, Cai Zhongxing, Yu Zhengjin, Liu Jinsheng, and Qian Afa, demanding a ransom of 200 yuan per person.

Looting Sand Barge: Xu Bingyuan, the owner of the Jin Hongtai five-masted sand barge, sailed between Shanghai and other ports, transporting goods. The Shanghai end was managed by the Yuelai Company's Yifeng Yong on Hankou Road. On the 9th of this month, the Jin Hongtai loaded a large quantity of soybean cakes and Chinese cabbage in Qingdao and set sail for Shanghai. On the morning of the 16th, it reached the waters off Sheshan and encountered two pirate ships that were returning from kidnapping people in Ningbo. At around 10:00 AM, they met the Jin Hongtai sand barge. Seeing that the sand barge was large, with five sails, the pirates decided to seize it. They sped up their two ships to catch up and then opened fire with Mauser pistols, ordering the Jin Hongtai to stop. The two pirate ships surrounded the sand barge from both sides. The twenty-eight pirates transferred the thirteen hostages they had kidnapped to the sand barge, along with their weapons and equipment. They then forced the captain of the sand barge, Liu Yuwen, and the old helmsman, Zhan Mei, to steer the ship north. They said that there was not much food on board, only enough for the pirates, and that the hostages would have to starve. They planned to wait for someone to come and ransom the ship for 5,000 yuan.

Unexpectedly Encountering the Lianxing: On the afternoon of the 17th, at 2:00 PM, the hostages had been starving for three meals and were exhausted. The sand barge had reached the Chenjiasha waters. At that time, the hostages were all driven onto the deck, while the pirates hid inside the cabin, with one or two on deck as lookouts. Suddenly, the Lianxing customs patrol ship arrived. Fearing exposure, the pirates threatened the captain, crew of fourteen, and the thirteen kidnapped people not to reveal their situation. If the patrol ship sent someone to investigate, they were to say that they were carrying goods north. If anyone revealed anything, they would be shot. The hostages all complied. When the Lianxing approached the sand barge, it sent four sailors, each carrying a rifle, and one Westerner, carrying a machine gun, on a motorboat. They boarded the sand barge to search for bandits or smuggled goods. The pirates remained hidden in the rear cabin and allowed the patrol ship's personnel to investigate.

Opening Fire to Resist Arrest: The patrol ship's sailors, noting that cargo ships traveling from point A to point B should have permits from each port, noticed that the permit stated the ship was traveling from Qingdao to Shanghai, but the ship was heading north, became suspicious and questioned them. The old helmsman, Zhan Mei, quietly reported that there were bandits on board. However, the pirates in the rear cabin overheard this and opened fire, firing about three or four shots. Seeing the situation, the sailors returned fire with four shots. The old helmsman was killed by the pirates. The sailors ordered the hostages on deck to retreat to the bow of the ship and raise their hands. Another Westerner brought the machine gun onto the sand barge and aimed it at the pirates in the rear cabin, preparing to fire. The pirates did not dare to resist. The sailors arrested three pirates on the spot and took them and the ten crew members onto the motorboat. The sailors and the Westerner also boarded the motorboat and left the sand barge, raising a flag to alert the patrol ship.

Patrol Ship Opens Fire: The crew on the patrol ship saw the signal and, after the motorboat had moved a safe distance away, opened fire with machine guns and cannons, bombarding the sand barge. They also fired sulfur bombs to set it on fire. The sand barge caught fire, and the pirates and the unrescued hostages had nowhere to escape, so they jumped into the sea to escape. The motorboat returned to rescue them, pulling three crew members from the sand barge, thirteen previously kidnapped hostages, and eight pirates from the water. Seventeen pirates were either killed or drowned, and the sand barge was destroyed. The body of the old helmsman, Zhan Mei, who was killed by the pirates, drifted away with the wreckage of the ship.

Captured Pirates Brought to Shanghai: The Lianxing patrol ship captured eleven pirates and rescued twenty-six kidnapped people. They sailed back to Wusongkou on the previous morning and telegraphed the customs water police, ordering all detectives to take a launch to Song to pick up the prisoners. After the pirates gave their names, including Chen Xingfu, Jiang Yulai, Zhang Cenqiu, Weng Banghuan, Xu Daofu, Wang Gongbai, Chen Xuechun, Jin Liangsa, Jiang Zhongbiao, Xu Yunbiao, and Xu Guibao, they were divided into two groups of hostages. The first group consisted of thirteen crab catchers and fishermen, and the eleven fishermen including Liu Chuxing (selling goods at Tuo Daxing Zhan), Shi Shengxia (Li Ayu selling goods), Tang Shunfa (Chen Amao selling goods), Xin Linsheng (Zhu Laizhou selling goods), Xin Ali (Ma Mingfu selling goods), Dong Linsheng (Lin Zhenghe selling goods), Yu Dingsong (Daxing Zhan selling goods), Cai Zhongxing (Xianglong Zhan selling goods), Yu Zhengjin (Wang Shengmao selling goods), Liu Jinsheng (Longxin Zhan selling goods), Qian Afa (Ma Axing selling goods). The second group consisted of the sand barge captain Liu Yuwen, Shi Jingui, Fang Zhaofu, and crew members Zhou Liansheng, Cui Bufa, Zhong Jintai, Chen Changzhi, Zhu Changqing, Wei Zhengshan, Zhou Hongyin, Wu Fumu, Chen Dianru, and Huang Qiaosheng, totaling thirteen people. One of the pirates, Jin Liangyu, had been shot in the right leg. After interrogation by the detectives, the eleven pirates were transferred to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for disposal that evening. The twenty-six hostages, along with Jin Liangmao, a wounded pirate previously captured by the Wenxing patrol ship, who had recovered from his injuries, were sent to the bureau for interrogation yesterday afternoon at 2 PM.

Yongxing Warship on Patrol

Pursues and Captures Qingbin Pirates

Over Ten Killed and Captured Alive

Rescues Squad Leader and Weapons

China News Agency reports that the Ningbo Association in Shanghai received reliable information yesterday that a freezer ship docked at Qingbin Island in Dinghai County the day before yesterday. The first independent squad of the local basic cadre team went to inspect it. They found three quick-firing guns, but the licenses were complete, and local people confirmed that it was a freezer ship, so they did not conduct a strict investigation. However, at 1:00 PM, more than ten people suddenly rushed out of the ship with various firearms, attacking the squad, killing one guard and one militiaman, and abducting squad leader Zhou Zhicheng, seizing all the weapons of the squad. They then sailed away on the freezer ship. The militiamen went to Puzi Lake to call for help. The Yongping warship happened to be patrolling nearby, so they requested the ship to pursue and rescue them. Five pirates were killed on the spot, six were captured alive, and four jumped into the sea. Squad leader Zhou Zhicheng was rescued, and all the weapons were recovered. The brigade headquarters received a telegram from the captain of the Yongping warship reporting the incident yesterday.

Judgment in French Concession Gambling Scam Case

Yang Yingchu Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment

Cai Baoshan Detained for Over Three Months and Fined

Yang Yingchu, a 58-year-old Cantonese residing at No. 13 Dakang Lane, Bai'er Road, French Concession, fabricated rumors due to extreme poverty. He claimed that the current French Consul-General, Meili Ai, was on leave to return to France, and the new Consul would revitalize the market by allowing the establishment of gambling dens in the concession, and that he could arrange to obtain the licenses. He colluded with fellow villagers Yang Dingguo, Pan Shucan, Wang Baiqing, Cai Baoshan from Pudong, and Zhu Zhenhua from Changzhou to spread the word and seek investors. The French police discovered the scheme and sent two translators from the anti-gambling squad, Jiang Futian and Li Xianyang, disguised as investors Hong Bingan and his accountant Zhang Zhongan, to the Dadongxin Hotel on Xixin Bridge Street and the Dafang Hotel on Zhengjia Muqiao Street on the 30th of last month and the 1st of this month. They gathered Yang and others to discuss investment plans. Yang and others claimed that a capital of one million yuan was required to organize the venture, and that there were only five licenses available, two of which had already been taken by a Mr. Sun, and that each license would cost 45,000 yuan in official fees. The two parties actually entered into a contract. When the contract was completed, police detectives lurking at the Dafang Hotel, including Hang Bingquan, Cai Zongyi, He Zongyu, and Zhu Junpei, arrested Yang Yingchu and six others, as well as suspects Fu Fengshan (from Guangdong) and Pi Xichun (from Henan), in Room 301 of the Dafang Hotel at around 8:00 PM on the 1st. They searched Yang Yingchu and Cai Baoshan's residence, finding documents related to the establishment of a lottery house, including articles of association and contracts. The police concluded the investigation and sent them to the Eighth Criminal Division of the Second Special District Court. Yang Yingchu and Cai Baoshan were charged with fraud as a habitual offense under Article 364 of the Criminal Code, while the other six defendants were charged with fraud under Article 363 of the Criminal Code. Judge Sun Pengya ruled that the charges against Yang and Cai were not under his jurisdiction and ordered them to be transferred to the local court for trial. On the morning of the 17th, Judge Zhang Chaozuo of the local court convened a hearing in the First Tribunal, where the defendants hired lawyers to defend themselves. The proceedings were concluded, and a verdict was awaited. The details of the interrogation have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, the verdict was announced. At noon, Judge Zhang went to the First Criminal Tribunal and ordered the defendants to be brought to court. Yang Yingchu was sentenced to six months of imprisonment for participating in an organization aimed at committing crimes. Cai Baoshan (same charge) was sentenced to three months of imprisonment. Wang Baiqing, Pan Shucan, Yang Dingguo, and Zhu Zhenhua (same charge) were each fined 200 yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment will be credited at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. If the fine is converted, each day will be calculated at three yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment will be credited at a rate of one day for three yuan of fine. The articles of association and regulations for the lottery house and the contract for the organization of the lottery house were confiscated. Fu Fengshan and Pi Xichun were found not guilty.

Maoli Steamer Arrives Safely in Shanghai Yesterday

Details of Foiled Pirate Attempt

Yili Also Arrives After Great Scare

The Maoli steamer of the Maoli Steamship Company, located at No. 4 Hengxin Lane, Outer Bund, Nanshi, left Shanghai on the 13th of this month (last Thursday). Pirates disguised as passengers hid in the cabins, attempting to hijack the ship mid-route. The ship arrived in Dinghai the next day at noon, where the water police discovered the pirates' weapons. The ship arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning. Further details are reported below:

First Mate Details the Incident: The Maoli steamer returned to Shanghai at 8:20 AM yesterday morning and docked at Pier No. 10 in Nanshi. A reporter from this newspaper visited the company and spoke with manager Miao Shuizhang. The Maoli's first mate was also present and was asked about the incident. According to him, the ship left Shanghai at 5:00 PM on the 13th, carrying over a hundred passengers. Around 9:00 AM the next morning, the ship arrived in Dinghai but did not dock, anchoring in the sea. The water police boarded the ship and discovered one male pirate, one female pirate, a 13-year-old girl, and a baby in the female pirate's arms. The female inspector found a wooden-cased pistol with fourteen bullets hidden in the female pirate's crotch. More than ten bullets were found in the male pirate's luggage. The water police questioned the pirate about whether there were any accomplices on board. The female pirate only stated that she was from Haimen Bei and that there were four others in Shanghai, but the Maoli steamer left an hour early that day, and they might not have been able to catch up and might have taken the Yili steamer to Wenzhou. The rest of her statement was evasive. She was taken to the police station by the water police for questioning.

Did Not Dare to Sail to Shipu: After the water police, together with the ship's police, conducted a thorough search of the passengers and luggage in the cabins, they allowed the ship to continue to Haimen and Huangyan at 5:00 PM that afternoon, escorted by police officers. However, they did not sail to Shipu Pier because of the previous accident involving the Xinhai Men steamer, where pirates boarded the ship. As they were wary, passengers and goods destined for Shipu were transferred to the Xinhai Men steamer. The Xinhai Men happened to be in Dinghai on the same day and met the Maoli steamer.

Today's Scheduled Sailing: The reporter from Datong News Agency requested to interview the ship owner, Xu Baosheng, but he had already disembarked. The reporter then visited manager Miao Shuizhang at the company. According to Mr. Miao, the ship had six escort police officers led by Captain Yang Baolian. Although the incident was unexpected, they were fortunate to escape danger. In the future, they will pay special attention to passengers with suspicious behavior to ensure safety. The scheduled sailing tomorrow (today) will proceed as usual, loading passengers and cargo and leaving at 5:00 PM for a certain port.

Yili Greatly Alarmed: The reporter from Datong News Agency then went to the Lianan Steamship Company at No. 16 Pu Guanqiao to inquire about the situation on the Yili steamer. The pirates captured in Dinghai revealed that there were four other accomplices on the Yili steamer bound for Wenzhou on the same day. The company received a telegram from Dinghai on the afternoon of the 14th, and the company sent a wireless telegram to the Yili steamer, warning them to be careful. They also sent a telegram to the Wenzhou branch, ordering them to quickly report to the local police and inspect the Yili in the Jiangxin area as soon as it arrived in Wenzhou without waiting for it to dock.

Thorough Search in Jiangxin, Wenzhou: When the Yili steamer arrived in Wenzhou at 2:00 PM on the 15th, the water police conducted a thorough search in the Jiangxin area, but found nothing. It is feared that the pirates may have disembarked mid-route, or secretly discarded their weapons. The Yili steamer also returned to Shanghai at 8:00 AM yesterday and will load passengers and cargo as usual today, sailing to the ports of Dinghai, Kanmen, Yueqing, and Wenzhou.

Railways Bureau Advises Fourth-Class Passengers

Pay Attention to Safety and Hygiene

Printed Popular Leaflets Distributed on Trains

Do Not Jump Off the Train Before It Comes to a Complete Stop

The Railways Bureau, in light of the numerous accidents that have occurred on trains, resulting in injuries and deaths, mostly due to passengers' carelessness, especially among fourth-class passengers, and the difficulty in maintaining cleanliness on fourth-class carriages, has assigned Liu Junming from the General Affairs Department and Hu Shisan from the Transportation Department to explain the dangers of jumping off trains and walking on the tracks to fourth-class passengers, as well as the importance of maintaining public hygiene on trains. The officers have prepared a "Notice to Fourth-Class Passengers" leaflet, printing 40,000 copies, to be distributed during lectures to promote awareness. The text of the leaflet is published below: (1) Do not get on or off the train before it has come to a complete stop. Jumping off the train can lead to serious injury or death. (2) Do not fall asleep on the train, as you may miss your stop. If you have already passed your stop, you can report to the ticket inspector. Do not jump off the train while it is in motion, as this can lead to serious accidents. (3) Passengers must purchase tickets according to regulations. Do not try to be clever, as taking shortcuts, such as jumping off the train or standing on the footboard outside the door, is very dangerous and not worth the risk. (4) Do not stand in the doorway or between carriages, as you may fall and be injured. (5) Do not stick your head out of the window, as you may be injured. (6) When walking along the railway tracks, be sure to move out of the way when you see a train approaching. Do not cross the tracks or walk near the tracks to avoid injury. People living near the railway tracks must strictly prohibit children from playing near the tracks to avoid accidents. (7) People with infectious or serious illnesses should not travel by train to avoid spreading the illness to others and worsening their own condition. (8) Everyone should help maintain the cleanliness of the toilets. Do not litter paper, fruit peels, or other waste. Gather them in one place for cleaning. (9) Do not spit, litter cigarette butts, or put your feet on the seats. (10) If you find anything unclean on the train, you can ask the attendant to clean it. If they refuse, you can report it to the railway officer on board for resolution.

Xinhai Men Steamer Crew and Passengers

Tragically Killed by Stray Bullets

Shipu Pirates Surrounded by Soldiers and Police

The Xinhai Men steamer of the Xinhai Men Steamship Company was hijacked by pirates en route from Yong to Wen. After the soldiers and police encircled and suppressed them, the pirates released all the kidnapped crew and passengers when they realized the situation was critical. As a result, some were killed by stray bullets, while others were rescued by the soldiers and police. The situation is as follows:

First Mate and Passengers Tragically Killed: After the incident, the Sixth Regiment of the Zhejiang Security Corps and the Second Water Police Team, along with the local military and police, launched an attack on the pirate's den near Yanshan, Niushenmen, Taizhou. The pirates resisted, but were overpowered by the soldiers and police. They released the kidnapped passengers and crew. The Xinhai Men steamer's first mate, Zhang Shixuan, son-in-law of ship owner He Shengzhang, and a passenger surnamed Jia, a graduate of Jinling University, were killed by stray bullets. Their bodies are being held in Haimen. The other crew and passengers were rescued safely.

Soldiers and Police Encircle: The soldiers and police have now implemented a large-scale encirclement, dispatching armed troops and land and water police to seal off the pirate-infested area near Shipu, aiming to eliminate the root of the problem. Therefore, the pirates, except for those who have already been killed, cannot escape.

Haixing Fishing Boat Captain

Beaten for Not Joining the Union

Chen Youtu and Others Accused of Assault

The Verdict Will Be Announced at Five O'Clock Today After Yesterday's Hearing

Xin Shanzhong, a Ningbo native and captain of the Haixing fishing boat, lived in the Guanqiao area of the Nanshi district. Because Xin had not joined the Fishing Boat Industry Workers' Improvement Association, Chen Youtu, the standing director of the association, along with several others, went to Xin Shanzhong's home around 6 or 7 PM on the 23rd of last month. They beat Xin and his wife, Zheng, and destroyed their belongings. Still not satisfied, they dragged Xin to the Fishing Boat Industry Workers' Improvement Association hall near Dongtingshan Alley. Upon hearing the news, the local police station quickly dispatched a large number of officers to the scene and arrested Chen Youtu, Le Junxie, Dai Shansheng, Yu Ruilian, Dong Afa, Le Huixiang, Yang Maogen, Zhu Bisheng, Zhou Pingying, Wang Yuesheng, and others who had committed the assault. Together with the injured Xin Shanzhong and Xin Zheng, they were taken to the police station and then transferred to the local court. Prosecutor Wu Deying proposed the case and interrogated them. After further summoning Shi Youxiao (also known as Youqiao) and others for questioning, it was determined that Chen Youtu, Le Junxie, Dai Shansheng, Le Huixiang, Yu Ruilian, Dong Afa, and Shi Youxiao should be detained on charges of assault, property damage, and restriction of freedom. The remaining individuals were released on bail pending further investigation. Yesterday morning at 10 AM, Guan Liting presided over the hearing in the tenth courtroom. The defendants, Chen Youtu and others, hired lawyers such as Yu Hualong to represent them in court. According to Xin Shanzhong's testimony, he was 37 years old and from Ningbo. He had just become the captain of the Haixing fishing boat on October 19th. Chen Youtu from the workers' union ordered me to join, but I refused. Chen Youtu gathered more than 40 people and rushed to my home, beating my wife and me and destroying all the items in my house. They also dragged my wife and me, along with my 12-year-old child Guangming, to the workers' union hall a good distance from my house. The injuries I sustained have not yet healed, and so on. Next, Xin Zheng testified that she was 30 years old, and the rest of her testimony was the same as her husband's. The judge ordered Chen Youtu to be brought to court for questioning. He was 42 years old, from Ningbo, and worked as a standing director in the fishing boat industry union, earning a monthly salary of 60 yuan. My union's duty is to mediate, so how could I instigate a crowd to commit violence? This lawsuit occurred because Xin Shanzhong was instructed by others. That day, dozens of people suddenly rushed to the union hall and destroyed the belongings, causing the glass on the premier's frame to fall and injure Xin's forehead. He denied the assault. Yu Ruilian testified that he was 32 years old, from Ningbo. That day, I was eating in the kitchen. When I heard the noise and went outside, I was arrested. I don't know anything else. Zhou Chuanhua was also mistakenly arrested and died of illness two days after being released on bail by the court. Dong Afa testified that he was 28 years old, from Ningbo, and made a living by fishing. That day, I went to the union hall to ask if there was any mail from home. They started arguing, and I got scared and hid, but I was caught by the police. Le Junxie testified that he was 34 years old, from Ningbo, and lived near Xiangyan Bridge. He worked as an inspector in the union, earning a monthly salary of ten yuan, and also denied the assault. Dai Shansheng testified that he was 27 years old, from Dinghai, and made a living by fishing. That day, I went to the union hall to find a friend and was mistakenly arrested. Le Huixiang testified that he was 28 years old, from Ningbo, and worked on a fishing boat. That day, after the fishing boat docked, I went to the union hall to visit friends and chat, and I was also arrested. Shi Youxiao testified that he was 28 years old, from Ningbo, and was a director in the union, responsible for collecting donations. There are seven directors in the union. I was not at the scene at the time. Later, I was summoned by the court. After hearing the testimony, the judge ordered Xin Shanzhong and Xin Zheng to identify Chen Youtu and others as the perpetrators in court. Xin Shanzhong also said that Shi Youxiao knocked out his teeth and that he was the main culprit. At this point, Prosecutor Wu Deying arrived in court and made his arguments. Then, the defense began. Lawyers Yu Hualong and Ma Yizhong rose to defend the defendants Chen Youtu and others for a long time. Finally, Dai Ningrui, the lawyer representing the plaintiff in the private prosecution, requested an additional 30 yuan and seven jiao for medical and funeral expenses, as well as compensation for other losses, and would file another lawsuit separately. The judge asked Chen Youtu how he would respond to the private prosecution. Chen replied that he was willing to pay compensation. The judge, considering the case to be clear, concluded the hearing and scheduled the verdict to be announced at 10 AM on the 15th. The seven defendants, including Chen Youtu, were returned to custody to await further instructions.

Water Company

Investigating Thefts of Water Meter Covers

Recently, the Nanshi Water Company has discovered that a large number of water meter covers installed in various households have been stolen. The covers are essential for protecting the meters, and once damaged, the meters lose their protection and must be replaced. The covers are made of copper, and the thieves steal them to sell to copper shops for money. However, the company has suffered significant losses. It is reported that the company has already petitioned the municipal authorities to investigate and punish the culprits, and has also posted rewards and issued leaflets to households. If the thief can be apprehended, a reward of 100 yuan will be given. For providing information leading to the arrest, a reward of 50 yuan will be given.

The Police Are Still Investigating

A Large Number of Armed Detectives Went to Arrest Him

Dai's Wife Lost Her Footing and Pleaded for Help

Dai Awu, a resident of No. 7 Zhizhong Li, Baliaoqiao Road (also known as West Xinqiao Street) in the French Concession, is about 30 years old. His wife, surnamed Mou, is in her twenties, with permed hair and fashionable clothes. They have a four-year-old son named Bao Bao and employ a nanny. The furniture in the house is all made of rosewood and sandalwood. Those who do not know them suspect that he is a wealthy merchant. When neighbors asked his wife what her husband did for a living, she falsely claimed that he was a comprador on a foreign ship. In fact, Dai has no occupation and specializes in robbery as a business, living lavishly and having disciples. Because the secret was not well kept, it was discovered by the French Concession Police. Yesterday (the 19th), at dawn, a large number of armed detectives were specially dispatched to arrest him at his address. The detectives were quiet and inconspicuous, driving a truck to the location and managing to enter No. 7. The detectives rushed upstairs to Dai's bedroom, where Dai Awu was fast asleep, and he was captured. His wife took the opportunity to escape to the drying platform and fled from the roof into the skylight of No. 6. Because the woman was anxious and panicked, she lost her footing and fell, suffering minor injuries and pleading for help. As a result, she was still arrested by the detectives. After a brief interrogation, they were both taken to the Lujiawan French Concession Police Station in a truck, awaiting transfer to the court for trial. It was also heard that the detectives found a handgun and dozens of bullets under the washbasin in Dai's bedroom, which were also taken back to the police station.

Cruel and Brutal Abuse of a Maidservant

Wooden Sticks, Rattan Canes, and Branding Irons All Prepared

Chen Wu's Behavior Is Truly Inhumane

Xu Xingbao, a 12-year-old girl from Changshu, was sold by her parents to a Cantonese woman named Chen Wu at No. 723 Tianqing Road as an adopted daughter last summer for 50 yuan. Unexpectedly, recently, if the girl made a slight mistake in her work, Wu would beat her with wooden sticks and rattan canes, leaving her body covered in injuries, and would also brand her back with a branding iron and strike her fingers with a small hammer. The girl, around 9 PM the day before yesterday, took a hot water bottle outside to get hot water from a nearby stove. She broke the bottle and cried on the way, not daring to return home. A patrolling Chinese constable investigated and learned the truth. He took her to the Hongkou Police Station. After a while, Wu came to the police station to look for Xu. She was detained, and a search of her bed resulted in the discovery of wooden sticks, rattan canes, and a branding iron and small hammer in the drawer. The police chief ordered her to send the girl to the orphanage and be held in custody. Yesterday morning, she was escorted to the First Special Court's Third Criminal Tribunal. Li Zhishan, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, stated the facts and said that Xu was examined at the Tongren Hospital and found to have branding iron marks on her back and waist, as well as countless scars on her arms and legs. The defendant was truly inhumane and should be severely punished. All the evidence was presented to the court. Xu testified that she called the defendant "aunt," but she was beaten with wooden sticks and rattan canes for not doing her work well. Sometimes she was beaten two or three times a day, or once every few days. If the laundry was not clean, her fingers, back, and waist would be struck with a hammer. About a week ago, she was branded with a branding iron. All of this was true. When questioned, Wu's testimony was evasive, admitting only that she had slightly hit her with a wooden stick because she had stolen money. Lawyer Li rose and said that Xu did not want to return to her hometown because her parents ate opium and were poor and had sold her. If she returned home, she would be treated the same way. He requested that she be temporarily sent to the Jiliang Institute for care. The court approved this. Judge Wu Zehan ordered Chen Wu to be returned to custody and scheduled a later date to review the case. Xu was to be re-examined by a forensic doctor to verify the injuries.

Zeng Yang's Motives Are Unsavory

Xu Yinxun's Behavior Is Despicable

Wei Hanchen, a native of Anhui residing at No. 14, Alley 87, Jing'an Temple Road, has been unemployed for a long time, resulting in poverty for his family. He entrusted his 16-year-old daughter, Liandi, to be a nanny at the home of Mrs. Dai Yin at No. 146, Alley 1238, Fuxu Road. Mrs. Zeng led her to the home of her lover, Xu Yinxun, at No. 18, Alley 990, Jia'zhi Road in the Nanshi district, intending to sell her. That night, Mrs. Zeng, Xu, and Wei Liandi slept in the same bed. Unexpectedly, in the middle of the night, Xu was suddenly overcome with lust and used violent means to rape Wei repeatedly. The girl was unable to resist and was violated. Ma Xiangbo Is Engaged in Mediation

There Is Still Hope for a Settlement

He then had Wang transported home, but medical treatment was ineffective, and she died on July 12th. The judge first questioned both parties about their age, origin, address, and occupation. The lawyer representing the appellant, Yan Yinwu, said that there was still hope for a settlement in this case and requested the court to postpone the hearing. According to the defense lawyer for the appellee, Mr. Ma Xiangbo came forward to mediate and issued a statement in the newspaper to clarify the misunderstanding between the two parties, but both parties were unwilling to bear the cost of the advertisement, which led to the suspension of the mediation. The judge said that the medical issues in the case needed to be investigated in detail, so he adjourned the hearing and ordered that it be rescheduled for further questioning. Then, the court adjourned.

Forging Collateral Receipts

Using Them to Deceive Creditors

Wu Xinglong Sentenced to Six Months' Imprisonment

Wu Xinglong, a native of Zhenjiang, has been working as a bookkeeper in hotels. Previously, he borrowed 100 yuan from his relative Gan Zhongchu. Recently, Gan was pressing him urgently for repayment, so he had a wild idea and forged a collateral receipt for 150 yuan from the Baohua Hotel, which is under the jurisdiction of the Wufu Travel Company, and mortgaged it to Gan. Recently, Gan was in urgent need of money, so he took the collateral receipt to Baohua Hotel to redeem the cash the day before yesterday morning. Xu Wenzhao, the manager of the hotel, examined it and realized that it was forged, so he asked where it came from and learned that it was given by Wu. He then went to find Wu. Xu Wenzhao thought that the amount of this receipt might not be the only one and that if he did not investigate it strictly, there would be more complications in the future, so he reported it to the Laozha Police Station, which ordered detective Chen Shanji to arrest Wu and take him back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special District Local Court's First Criminal Tribunal. Ru Baoyi, the lawyer for the police station, stated the facts of the case and filed a public prosecution based on the crime of forging documents under Article 224 of the Criminal Code. Then, Xu Wenzhao testified, proving that the receipt was forged and requesting that he be punished according to the law. When questioned, Wu Xinglong said that he was in financial difficulty and that Gan was urgently demanding repayment, so he had no choice but to resort to this tactic, but the receipt was forged by a Mr. Huang. Judge Feng Shide, after reviewing the testimony, sentenced Wu Xinglong to six months' imprisonment for forging documents as a warning.

Rickshaw Industry Representatives Petitioned the City Government Yesterday

The Public Utilities Bureau Detained Publicly Owned Licenses

Requesting Their Return to Maintain the Livelihoods of Rickshaw Pullers

In the rickshaw industry in this city, there is a type of license that is publicly owned. These licenses were handed over to the Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Association by the Public Utilities Bureau of the municipal government in 1928 for management, leased to poor tenants, and the license fees obtained were used for the public welfare expenses of rickshaw pullers. This year, in August, Ju Ganxin, a member of the rickshaw industry association, reported to the Public Utilities Bureau that the 64 publicly owned licenses were now in the hands of general large rickshaw businesses and that the license fees obtained were not being used for public welfare purposes. The Public Utilities Bureau, based on the report, detained the licenses and stopped issuing them. Subsequently, after mediation by the rickshaw industry association and with Ju's understanding, the Public Utilities Bureau withdrew the complaint. However, the Public Utilities Bureau stated that the vehicles using these licenses were mostly old and damaged and would only be issued after the vehicles were replaced. However, the license holders and the rickshaw industry association believe that the licenses have been suspended for three months, and those who rely on these licenses for a living include the rickshaw pullers and their families, totaling several hundred people. Prolonging the detention would cause extreme hardship to their lives. Therefore, at 11 AM yesterday morning, Zhang Huaiyang and Wang Rongqing, representatives of the rickshaw industry association, Zhang Wenhua and Lu Jinyu, representatives of the license holders, and Yuan Hongjun, a representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, jointly petitioned the municipal government. Zhu Weiyao was dispatched by the municipal government to receive them and promised to forward their request to the municipal government's rickshaw research committee for proper handling. The representatives then left one after another. Zhang Huaiyu, a standing committee member of the rickshaw industry association, also said that since the 64 licenses were detained by the Public Utilities Bureau, those who relied on these licenses for a living had lost their means of support, which has been the case for three months. In fact, these licenses are not manipulated by large rickshaw businesses, but are leased out through large rickshaw businesses. Currently, to maintain the livelihoods of the rickshaw pullers, they have decided to continue to request the rickshaw research committee to return the licenses.

Continued Arrests of Robbers in the Dalin Road Robbery Case

Following the robbery of a large sum of money and gold jewelry from the home of Jiang Heshang (also known as Jiang Changfu) at No. 1, Alley 18, Dalin Road in the Nanshi district the day before yesterday, the Sangguantang Police Station reported it to the Ximen Branch. Two Route Party Headquarters Sent Personnel to Reorganize the Two Route Trade Unions

According to the Central News Agency, the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Trade Unions have been established since September 1931, more than three years ago. The organizations have not been sound, so the work cannot be promoted. Last December, they also planned to end on their own and requested the superior to send personnel to reorganize. The special party headquarters of the road at that time considered the situation to be tense and the labor movement could not be interrupted, and reported to the Central People's Movement Guidance Committee for approval, ordering the trade union to continue to be responsible, and must prepare for re-election in the shortest period of time, but it has not been implemented to this day. The two special party headquarters of the road deliberated again and again, and deeply thought that the organization of the association cannot be expected as before. Prolonging it like this, not only will guidance be difficult, but it will also hinder the future of the labor movement. Therefore, on the 18th of the day before yesterday, the 96th executive committee meeting was convened, and it was decided to reorganize the organization and implement the reorganization in accordance with the central regulations on the reorganization of people's organizations. It is now learned that Zhang Yunhe, Zhang Ji, and Chen Junpei were appointed as instructors, and Pan Qin, Hong Desheng, Luo Lairong, Xue Jie, and Yuan Qiaofu and other five people were appointed as reorganizers. Yesterday, they were ordered to stop activities immediately. The reorganization period is limited to two months to complete the official re-election and the establishment of the trade union. They immediately reported to the Central Executive Committee's People's Movement Committee and Organization Committee for record, and sent a letter to the Ministry of Railways and the Two Route Administration Bureau for investigation.

To the esteemed Editor, I am writing to you regarding the news article "Major Fraud Case of Opening a Gambling Den in the French Concession" published in your newspaper yesterday (18th).
