Free Talk

My Views on "The Relationship Between Work and Life"

— Xian He

The relationship between work and life is very close, which is almost a universally acknowledged fact. However, a few days ago, Mr. Zhou Yuying put forward three points of view to express his opposition, and his arguments are worthy of high discussion. Therefore, I also briefly write down a few points to ask Mr. Zhou for correction.

The first point is that Mr. Zhou puts forward the importance of "imagination." He said, "Imagination constitutes the substance of literature, and develops passionate emotions丨through certain thoughts and feelings." He also said, "Imagination only has the distinction between profound, smooth, and superficial, bad, and there is absolutely no distinction between substantial or insubstantial life." It can be seen that Mr. Zhou opposes the need for a substantial life, and the impact of a substantial life on imagination. If according to this statement, then a writer only needs to have a strong imagination, and he can sit in the "pavilion or mansion" to write, because imagination will develop passionate emotions, and literature is "after all a discipline centered on emotion," isn't this very convenient? But is it really that simple in reality? No matter how rich the imagination of a writer is, if there is no experience of real life, then what kind of tricks can he imagine out of thin air in his empty head? Mr. Zhou said on the one hand, "However, imagination cannot be separated from the general reality of life," but on the other hand, he denied the close relationship between substantial or insubstantial life and profound or insubstantial imagination, which is really incomprehensible. The poems of Homer and the novels of Tolstoy are only the crystallization of their imagination, or are they reflections of the social life of their time, which can be verified by historical facts. As for Mr. Zhou's belief that "the element of thought was added to literature only with the emergence of modern progressive literature," as if all previous works were just a chaotic mass of emotions, abstract and irrelevant, is this really the case? Are the writers before the so-called "modern times" just some simple little kids who have nothing to do, only know joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness, only know how to wipe their noses and shed tears?

In the second paragraph, Mr. Zhou cited many writers from China and abroad. He said that the works of Mao Dun and Ye Shaojun are not entirely records of private life, which is very correct. However, Mr. Zhou sometimes interprets "actual life" only as narrow "private life," and sometimes separates them mechanically, which is an incorrect view. Because man is a social animal, his social relations are very complex. In addition to his own direct experience, there is also a broader, larger-scale "general life." The so-called "experiencing life" does not necessarily mean "private life experienced personally," but the so-called "substantial life" precisely requires a writer to have life knowledge in all aspects, thorough and complete life knowledge. A writer must liberate himself from the narrow circle of private life and broaden his horizons. He must be good at observing all kinds of life, and he must have a clear understanding of the themes he chooses. To mechanically understand "direct life experience" is easy to mislead people. In fact, it is impossible to directly experience everything personally. However, the life that has been personally experienced can be written more intimately and movingly, which is always the truth. Even the "observation" I am talking about is by no means an abstract method. Mr. Zhou does not understand from these aspects, but abandons the social environment in which the writer is located, all social relations, and does not base on a historical point of view, and asks Balzac, who is not "modern," and not an artistic ability to describe other kinds of stories, "like Sinclair's depiction of the destruction of an oil tycoon, the misery of coal mines and slaughterhouses," which is indeed as Mr. Zhou himself said: "I'm afraid it's an unreasonable request"?

As for the third point, Mr. Zhou's emphasis is still on "imagination." However, he himself also said: "...forced to imagine social affairs in the pavilion or mansion, people with strong imagination can write a little bit of something that seems to be true, and people with naive imagination can only foolishly say crazy things, and completely lose authenticity," which shows the unreliability of "imagination." If a writer wants to strengthen his "imagination," so that his "imagination" does not become a vague "fantasy," so that his works can only reach the realm of "seeming to be true," or even completely lose authenticity, then he must 丨again borrowing Mr. Zhou's own words丨 not be separated from the general reality of life. In other words, he must bravely and actively "participate in life," "experience life," and "enrich life." Therefore, Mr. Zhou's "dissent" did not cancel the importance of "substantial life" for "profound thinking," but instead strengthened the meaning. However, when drawing conclusions, Mr. Zhou made a strange turn, abstractly putting forward the "question of the writer's ability," saying that the success or failure of a work depends entirely on the writer's ability. I do not oppose the writer's "ability," but ability is not some mysterious magic weapon, and it can never be put forward in this way out of thin air, let alone reverse cause and effect, and give it an absolute and decisive meaning. Mr. Zhou also seems to oppose those myopic writers who only write about trivial matters around them, saying that their writing method is "opportunistic," which is also true, but I have already said that we must never think that grasping a little bit of fragmentary experience 丨 personal private life, is considered "substantial" and "experiencing." We cannot overlook the difference between "experiencing" and "experience."

In short, I think the "theory of writer's ability" is untenable. If we talk about abstract and mysterious "ability" divorced from real life, then it is inevitable to be empty talk.

"The Disease of Worldliness"

— Yang Shiji

Liu Rongqi praised Wang Mojie's poems, saying that they had no "disease of worldliness." The disease of worldliness he pointed out is: "Relying on talent and learning, making an identity, and being good at climbing." I think these three items can also be used to criticize the general situation of today's literary and artistic circles, although the morbid state of the disease of worldliness is definitely not limited to this.

Relying on talent and learning was originally a title that many people hoped to win, because having talent to rely on and having learning to display, how proud it should be! As the trend spreads, all those with a little cleverness show off their faces of talented scholars. In today's literary and artistic circles, if we find one or two better productions, or one or two more insightful and refreshing arguments, then we can see the author promote his great principles of what Ism, and then look down with haughty eyes, as if he has ascended the sandalwood niche. The affected madness of that state is as尊大的 as the wandering knights who have traveled all over the Three Mountains and Five Mountains. However, the technique of subconsciously pursuing this head weighing is not very simple. For example, if I want to stand out, I can deliberately make eccentric views to shock the world; I can also hold one thing, one object, or one person as an enemy and vigorously destroy its actual achievements; I can also create something out of nothing and create some bold and satisfying anecdotes for myself. I can also use sweet words to confuse the public, saying that this place "encompasses everything and has everything." These are all able to directly or indirectly show one's talent and erudition.

Writing here, I think it is worthwhile to consider whether "talent" exists in today's world; but we can say that perhaps the level of physiological aptitude is what is called talent, and the ugly state of those heroes who have meager talent and want to display their learning naturally cannot avoid the criticism of small feet and large shoes.

If the decoration of talent and learning can be exaggerated and used as the purpose of some people, then "making an identity" is one of the means to achieve this purpose. The impact of identity on my way of being a person is so great that there are examples everywhere that can be picked up. The solemn and moral appearance of the gentry class is the identity they pride themselves on; the petty and vulgar appearance of the common people is the identity assigned to them by those above. Such identities are permanently established! The gap between them in terms of nobility and inferiority; and what is the identity of talented scholars! There are many categories of talented scholars, so their identities are also different. Under the myriad of states, they generally strive to dress up according to each person's desires, just like acting. Those who play pure roles must paint Zhu Moqi, those who play dan roles must apply powder and grease, those who play the King of Chu must have a leopard jaw and tiger whiskers, and those who play the Prime Minister of Han must wear a lun towel and feather fan, otherwise they will not be consistent with the role they play. Accordingly, "romantic," "elegant," "crazy," and "sick" are used to the greatest extent and become the best tools for our talented scholars to soar.

"Being good at climbing" is complementary to making an identity. Although someone has broken through "my friend ××," "our predecessor Yuan Hongdao" has still not been heard. To have an identity, you must climb to consolidate your foundation and increase your crown. The reason is obvious, why bother, but what is surprising is the awkwardness of the reverse in words and deeds.

This article is just the leftovers of Qi, making unnecessary annotations, which is also ultimately caused by the psychology of climbing.

Cowpox and Anesthesia (Continued)

— Qiao Feng

Equally famous in the history of science and medicine, and even more similar to cowpox in terms of the benefits of life, is the discovery of anesthesia. The more developed the nervous system of an animal, the more afraid it is of pain. Although the power to fear and endure pain will vary due to individual physique, customs, and ideas, there is no doubt that humans are the most afraid of pain. Before anesthesia was discovered, major surgery could not be performed, and even opening a boil would cause the patient great pain. Now with anesthesia, very serious surgeries can be treated.

The discovery of anesthesia is commonly attributed to Morton, a dentist in Boston, USA, in 1846. However, tracing its history is very ancient. Europe had occasionally used anesthesia in ancient times: sometimes hemp and sometimes mandrake. Italy in the thirteenth century used a kind of mandragora as an anesthetic. The Polish King Augustus also used anesthesia when performing surgery in 1782, but in ancient times, it was sometimes used and sometimes not. Its widespread use like today was after Morton's discovery.

Before this, in 1787, Sir Humphry Davy, experimented on himself, inhaling the gaseous compound called "laughing gas." Although he did not inhale it to the point of losing consciousness, he believed that laughing gas could be used as an anesthetic and could be used for surgical operations.

In 1818, another celebrity, Faraday, said that the gas of ether could anesthetize people. Later, several doctors in the United States also said so, but it was not widely adopted.

After several years, in 1844, Wells, a dentist from Connecticut, USA, used laughing gas to extract teeth, but the result was not very successful. His courage disappeared and he did not try again. He wanted to use ether instead and tried it himself, but he felt uncomfortable and gave up.

Although Wells' experiment failed, he told the dentist Morton in Boston about this. Morton was very enthusiastic about this matter and felt that ether was better than laughing gas, so he used ether to experiment. He not only experimented with animals, but also experimented with tooth extraction. The results of his experiment convinced him that ether could be used as a good anesthetic. In 1846, he told the surgeon Warren in Boston about this and asked for the opportunity to test his discovery when the opportunity arose. So, in the Massachusetts General Hospital, ether was used as an anesthetic to remove a tumor on a patient's neck, and the result was very good. Since then, the use of ether as an anesthetic has gradually become popular.

The discovery that ether can be used as an anesthetic was actually not only Morton. At about the same time, the chemist Jackson in Boston also discovered that ether could be used as an anesthetic. And Dr. C. Long, a doctor in a small town in Georgia, used ether as an anesthetic in the spring of 1842 and also removed a tumor on a patient's head, and continued to apply it afterwards. Only because Morton's experiment was known the most and spread more widely, therefore, when it comes to the discovery of anesthesia, his name is often mentioned.

After the discovery that ether could be used as an anesthetic was published, Sir James Simpson, a surgeon in Scotland, knew that someone in France had used chloroform as an anesthetic when experimenting with animals, so he took it to experiment and found that the results of chloroform used in surgical operations were good. So, in addition to ether, chloroform was added as another anesthetic.

There are many other discoveries that are beneficial to life. I have only said a little bit here. Future people will progress and no longer waste their efforts on opium, playing cards, and various gambling games, nor will they waste their energy on "fighting for land" and plundering money, and no longer think about ways to kill people with blood-red eyes; transferring the power used in useless and harmful aspects to various explorations and inventions will definitely be able to discover many things and methods that are extremely beneficial to life. This is a matter of course. (The End)

Give Life a Kick

— Ding

After reading Mr. Gu Xi's article "Give Life a Slap in the Face," I felt very sympathetic, and I also felt that it should be given a good kick.

Yes, to life, we "should take a tough attitude," 丨"as if we are not just slapping it in the face!" Because丨

This era is an era of suffering, an era of struggle. Living in this era, we should have a rising spirit to deal with our lives.

We not only need to have the burning emotions of a prairie fire, but also to experience, suffer, train, and build in our lives.

The national crisis is approaching us step by step. Who is willing to crawl under shackles, who will always be a slave?

However, who is willing to be a slave?

The raging tide of the times is roaring. We must advance with this turbulent wave.

Perhaps this huge tide will engulf us.

Perhaps this huge tide will crush us.

Perhaps this huge tide will wash us up to the high peaks of the mountains and the distant corners of the earth.

Perhaps this huge tide will surge us to a land of freedom and glory!

However, no matter what, in this era, from a personal point of view, we are just a tiny bubble in the huge tide, a speck of dust in the universe. However, from a general point of view, we gather together, and this is a majestic giant!

At this moment, everything around us is not full of ugliness, cruelty, disasters, troubles, darkness, poverty, hunger...?

What else can we miss?

We should take responsibility.

Although the road is rugged, steep, distant, and difficult.

But there will always be a time to reach it!

The Slave of Cosmetics

Tomorrow (2) (10) (1)

— Written by (Joseph Conrad), translated by Wu Xiangyu

"Stop," she cried loudly. "Don't go away."

Her head was lowered, and she listened attentively. She could not distinguish whether it was the fierce attack of the wind, or whether it was his fateful footsteps that were hurting her heart. Soon all sounds became inaudible. She also seemed to turn into a stone person. This deep, heavy, silent fear came to her heart丨丨more terrible than the fear of death. She raised her gradually disappearing strength for the final cry:

"Harry!"

Even the echo of the diminishing footsteps was gone. Everything was gone. The surging of the waves, the sound of the ever-flowing sea itself also seemed to stop. There was no sound丨丨-no sign of life, as if she were alone, lost alone in that stony place she had heard of, where those madmen went to seek gold and abandon their gold mines.

Captain Hagberd, in his dark room, had been paying attention. A window was opened again; in the silent air of this seemingly stony place, a voice echoed above her, high in the dark air丨丨the voice of crazy lies and despair-but also the voice of perpetual hope: "Is he gone丨that informer? Did you hear him say anything, my dear?"

She suddenly burst into tears. "No! No! No! I won't listen to him anymore," she sobbed.

He began to laugh triumphantly. "Did you scare him away? Good girl. Now we will be as before. Don't be impatient, my dear. Wait one more day."

In another cottage, old Carvil sat in a circle chair placed next to a spherical lamp on a near table, turning it very proudly, and shouted loudly to her in a fierce voice: "Bethan! Bethan! You, Bethan!"

Finally, she heard it, and as if controlled by fate, she began to silently walk towards her gloomy little hell-like room. This hell had no high doorposts, no terrible inscriptions deprived of hope - and she did not know what crime she had committed.

Captain Hagberd gradually fell into a state of mad joy above.

"Roll in! Don't make noise!" She rebuked him from the door below with tears on her face.

Because he thought that "something was wrong" before, and finally he was relieved, he was very happy, so he did not listen to her command. In this way, the old man's cry of forever believing in "tomorrow" seemed as if all the hopeful fantasies in the world had erupted and brought terror to her heart. (The End)

Supplement to the Shanghai Shenbao

Talk

Raising a Fat Son

— BORED

On the 16th, a telegram from Santa Monica, USA: "Screen goddess Clara Bow gave birth to a child in a local hospital today, weighing eight pounds. Her husband, Rex Bell, is also a screen star." Since she is a married woman, it is natural for her to give birth. Therefore, giving birth is originally a very ordinary thing. Now, the American female star Clara Bow has given birth to a big, fat son, which is worth such attention from newspaper reporters, sending telegrams to publicize it. "Isn't this going too far?"

"When men and women unite, all things are created." This is the natural principle of creation. Even in the United States, the number of small citizens born every day is countless, most of which are unheard of. However, special attention is paid to the birth of a small star, almost equivalent to the president giving birth to a small president, or the crown prince giving birth to a small prince. From this, we can see the worship of celebrities by beauties.

In our country, a Jiangbei woman, carrying a basket in one hand and a stick in the other, begs from door to door, singing her "Lotus Fall." Suddenly, she feels a burst of pain and discomfort in her stomach. She gives birth to a small beggar by the corner of someone's wall. She wraps him up herself, holding him by her side, unnoticed by anyone. Soon after, she continues to beg from door to door. This is also the birth of a big, fat son.

There are also the "big bosses" and "small bosses" who, no one knows which concubine number, suddenly "have the joy of a son" or "get a son on the first try." Therefore, they send out invitations widely, treat their guests lavishly, holding what kind of Tangbing feasts or Zuipan banquets. Distinguished guests fill the seats, and the sounds of congratulations overflow the house. The relatives and friends inevitably spend a lot of money, offering gifts, goldware, silk, each according to the thickness of their affection and what they can afford. It is truly a grievance and a waste.

As the saying goes, "Don't look at a child's birth, only look at the harvest in old age." Because the length of life is unpredictable, and death and longevity are even more uncertain. Moreover, the big, fat son born, will he be an important person in the future? A thief? A heroic soldier? A headline-grabbing star? Or a beggar begging from door to door? It is difficult to predict. In this way, what is the value of a big, fat son after all? When he is first born, how can we predict his future results? Then, celebrating his birth is absolutely meaningless.

Currently, in our country, the economy is declining, the rural areas are bankrupt, commerce is withering, and livelihoods are becoming increasingly difficult. It is difficult to maintain one's own life, and it is even more difficult to bear the burden of children. Therefore, there are many who raise children but do not keep them, or who raise them and send them to orphanages. In this case, is giving birth to a child really something to celebrate? Or something to mourn? It is still unknowable.

Once children are born, they must be educated. If they are not educated, they will either become beggars or bad elements of society. In our country, the number of people who can receive higher education is already small. Not only higher education, but even the cost of education for an ordinary junior or senior high school graduate is considerable. If the authorities do not pay attention to such aristocratic education and let "school bosses" raise prices, I am afraid that in the future, not only will there be no one who can receive higher education, but it will also be quite difficult to receive lower education. In this way, the quality of citizens will be even more uneven, and the national culture will decline day by day. Giving birth to sons and raising daughters is the most worrying thing in life. Alas!

Exile

— YEFI

It was an early winter evening. The electric lights in the station were brightly lit, and the noisy voices filled the entire station. All kinds of people were constantly moving around. Porters were busy grabbing luggage from passengers, and many vendors were stretching their voices to sell things. Several patrolmen and soldiers, each holding a whip, were patrolling back and forth inside and outside the station. In front of the fourth-class ticket window, a large group of not-so-pretty people were crowding; only a bunch of heads could be seen fluctuating under the intense electric light, a scene reminiscent of the starving masses in front of a soup kitchen.

The girlfriend also squeezed up, and with great difficulty, bought two and a half fourth-class tickets to Shanghai. He clutched the tickets, carrying a bag, shouldering a bedding roll. His wife also carried a basket of miscellaneous items, holding their son, Agou, and walked towards the ticket inspection point. But the ticket inspector insisted on making things difficult for them, saying that such a large bedding roll could not be brought onto the train. After his repeated pleas, they were finally allowed to pass. Passing through an underpass to the opposite platform, there were so many fourth-class passengers, but they were all like them, supporting the old and carrying the young, fleeing from their disaster-stricken hometown.

This was an 8:07 slow train for third and fourth class, but now it was almost 9 o'clock, and the train had not yet arrived. People were getting noisy, and Agou was clamoring for dinner. Although his mother and father were also really hungry, they had only drunk a bowl of thin porridge and eaten a few sweet potatoes when they left home in the morning. They hadn't even had cold water since then, so their stomachs were naturally rumbling uncomfortably. But where could they find dinner now? Listening to other children crying and clamoring in the same way.

"Agou, be good, don't make noise. We'll go to Shanghai to eat noodles, don't cry!" Agou's mother coaxed him painfully. When he heard about eating noodles, he put a dirty hand into his little mouth and sucked on it, a glimmer of hopeful smile on his thin face. But after a while, he seemed to feel disappointed again, and the thought of not having a broken thatched home emerged from his small heart.

"Mom! Why don't we go back? Go home to sleep!" he cried to his mother.

Caiyou was thinking about the home that had been attacked by natural and man-made disasters, and he couldn't help but feel some moisture in his eyes. Looking at his wife, looking at the ignorant and unfortunate child, he thought, if they could make a living in their hometown, why would they have to flee to the unfamiliar Shanghai? When they got to Shanghai, they would be without relatives or friends. How would they arrange things? Wouldn't starving to death in Shanghai be the same as starving to death at home? They only brought four dollars and eighty cents when they set off, and now, after deducting the travel expenses, they had less than three dollars left. What to do? As he thought this, he felt that a terrifying barrier had blocked his view, and he couldn't see what kind of world lay ahead. He didn't dare to think any further. If he couldn't find work in Shanghai, wouldn't he starve to death just the same! Well, starving to death in Shanghai would be better than starving to death at home. Anyway, in this day and age, there's no way for us poor people to survive!

He glanced weakly at his wife's worried face. The child had already fallen asleep in her arms. Although he was wearing a tattered cotton-padded jacket, it was ultimately too tattered, and the coldness still pricked his skin like needles.

The train rumbled and ran over, stopping with a "嘎!" sound beside the platform. After a while of shouting and squeezing, he and his two sons were also packed on board, which woke up Agou in her arms.

"Mom! Dad! I want to go home and eat!" Agou cried out again, oblivious to the situation.

Only Made Five Hundred and Some Odd Cash

— YIAN

A Snapshot

— CUNYIN

On the street, three people walked in desolation. There were no rickshaws, nor a police officer with his head tucked in.

"Dad! I can't walk anymore."

The child's cold hand tugged at his father's clothes.

"Child! We'll be at Uncle's house soon. Don't bother your dad. Come here, let me carry you!"

She picked up the eight-year-old child.

The father's face was flushed with heat. He carried two boxes with all his might, walking on the street.

"Mom! Why is the city so deserted?"

The child, nestled on his mother's shoulder, asked.

"On cold nights, the city is just like our countryside."

"Then, Dad lied! He said that the city is always colorful, morning and night."

"Don't talk so much! Cold wind will blow into your mouth, and you'll cough!"

"Mmm."

He pursed his lips and agreed. And then, even more silence.

After a while, he fell soundly asleep.

Two pairs of feet walked on the street. There were no shouts of selling evening newspapers, nor those selling sweet rice porridge.

"Ah, just one more turn, and we're there!"

The man sighed and said.

One turn, two turns, they had already been walking for a day! In the morning, after cleaning up at home, the family started out. They didn't have lunch, and they didn't have money to buy dinner, so they had to walk on empty stomachs.

They were all thinking of their uncle!

Their uncle was a living god of wealth. He would help them find a job. If it weren't for their uncle, they would starve to death if they stayed at home! The last resort was to go to their uncle who lived in the city!

"Heaven may not bless us, making us suffer to this point. But, it still has a bit of conscience, giving me an elder brother."

She thought. Her heart felt relieved.

"I remember! The first house, the second house, yes, this one!"

He put down the burden. He hurried to knock on the door.

"Who's there?"

After knocking for a while, someone finally came to ask.

"We're here to see Zhao Afu!"

"Zhao Afu? He doesn't live here anymore."

"Hmm? How can he not live here?"

"He robbed someone's things and was locked up in prison!"

"..."

The two people stood outside the door, looking at each other. They didn't say anything. The person inside didn't make a sound either.

After a moment, the woman knocked on the door and said:

"What? What... when will he be released?"

The sound of snoring inside was faintly transmitted!

"Hey! Don't knock on the door anymore!"

The husband said, sitting on the steps in disappointment.

×

It was another night.

The wife, dressed very prettily, her face covered with powder, stood on the street corner with many other women. An old woman followed her. She put on a smiling face, facing the male pedestrians. Sometimes, she would open her mouth like this.

"Hey! Want to come to my place and have some fun?"

This voice was filled with shame and pain!

In a dark alley, the husband and child were eating buns.

"Dad! Where did Mom go?"

"She went back to the countryside to get you some cotton clothes."

The dad, deceiving an innocent child.

"Mom also likes to eat these buns!"

"..."

"Dad, why are you crying?"

"Child! I'm not crying! My eyes just hurt! Hey, why aren't you eating?"

"I won't eat! I'll save these two for Mom!"

He obediently hid them in his pocket.

The dad looked at him, and couldn't help but shed another string of tears!

Amateur Mailbox

Bullying the Weak is Most Shameful

— EDITOR

Editor:

Last spring, I entered a foreign goods store of the Lianjia chain as an apprentice. Soon after entering the store, I was greatly bullied by the owner's two sons. Sometimes they would hit me, sometimes they would pat me, or spit phlegm on me. Their various unreasonable actions were really unbearable. If I told the owner (their father), I was afraid of causing bad results, so I was very sad. Yesterday afternoon, I was sitting in a chair, and they ran over again, for no reason took a very long yardstick, and hit me in the body. One of them shouted to hit me. I was hit five or six times, and I couldn't bear it, so I snatched the yardstick and didn't let them hit me. Unexpectedly, they immediately started crying, so the owner ran out and scolded me, saying that I was bullying them, which really made me feel wronged and had nowhere to go. At that time, I was stimulated by this and really wanted to commit suicide, but then I thought that it was not worth committing suicide for such a small matter, so I did not do it. However, how can I deal with such an environment? Sir, please give me an answer! Respectfully wishing you peace. Sincerely, Bao Shan

Editor's Note: Bullying the weak is a common phenomenon in society. In all different social strata, such things happen. Bao Jun's current experience is just one of the most minor ones.

We want to advise Bao Jun not to worry too much about this matter. If you think it is a great shame and want to commit suicide, that is even more unwise. Because children are ignorant, why bother arguing with such children? Even if you resist them and win, what is the point? So for this matter, you can only be patient temporarily, or find a way to avoid meeting them, and they will have no way to bully you.

Of course, if you think that the current painful environment is unbearable, then you can ask someone to find another job and try to change the environment. However, before finding a suitable position, it is best to be patient for the sake of job skills.

On the other hand, we must say that bullying the weak is really a most shameful thing, and people with this bad habit should actively correct their mistakes. Especially in childhood, this bad psychology cannot be developed. We hope that people will pay attention to this point. Finally, we also hope that Bao Jun and others who are bullied by others will not vent the pain they are suffering now on others when they have power in the future. This meaningless revenge is also unacceptable.

To Liang Chongyu, Lianxin, The Injured, Xie Ren, Cao, Qiuxia, Lu Ying, Mrs. Fang Chen, Biyun, Liu Renjing, Pingying, Shi, Zhang Yanfan, Liu Jianying, gentlemen: Please indicate the mailing address so that we can reply.

Ballad

Chen Ruilin's Mao Family Book

Yuan Chang (1120) 5:30 PM to 6:15 PM

Opening: "Idle Talk of the Examination Hall" (Part 3)

Examination candidates are particularly arrogant, consulting diviners to relieve their worries.

Fortune-tellers blindly flatter them, predicting certain success this year with incessant chatter.

Leaving the hall after grading papers during the Mid-Autumn Festival, each examiner praises the high quality of the essays presented.

They enjoy the moon and raise their cups, celebrating with unrestrained drinking all night long.

Internal and external corruption are strictly separated, carefully preventing any potential scandals.

Attention must be paid to the chief examiner's words, as the supervisors frequently arrive to obstruct.

Only when the Double Ninth Festival arrives do they wait for the list of successful candidates, and the announcement of literary fame involves much deliberation.

Once they unexpectedly achieve their soaring ambition, they can proudly wear their embroidered robes.

Loud gongs and drums announce the good news, and their names are marked on gilded red paper.

Wearing down an iron inkstone is no easy feat, but they enjoy the pleasure of their sons receiving official appointments and their wives being granted noble titles.

Those who fail the exam bitterly complain in vain, as ten years of studying vanish like smoke.

They must wait three years to retake the exam, hoping to be noticed in the current dynasty.

(Endless are) the countless idle talks of the examination hall, which I describe with my pen as fleeting clouds.

Wealth and fame are ultimately illusory, and life is like a dream, a sigh of drifting.

(It's better to) retire to the Eastern Mountain with a leisurely spirit, abandoning all worldly pursuits in the field of power and profit, enjoying peaceful years with wine in hand.

Zhou Jianhong's Big Red Robe

Central-Western (1040) 11:45 AM to 12:30 PM

Opening: "Urging Donations for Disaster Relief" Author: Willow

Alas, the suffering of the rural villages is unbearable, as disaster strikes again this year after last year's calamity.

The merciless sun shines across the land, turning the earth into a scorched, drought-stricken wasteland.

Causing the farmers to cry out in distress from every household, with no harvest of grain in the fields.

Some have not lit their stoves for a long time, while others support the old and carry the young, their faces covered in tears.

Some compete to strip bark from trees to fill their bellies, while others lie starving in bed, unable to speak.

Their voices are tragic, and their tears flow freely; when will this suffering end?

On this side are the fortunate ones who have not suffered disasters, able to rest peacefully without worry.

On that side are corpses scattered on roads and streets, filling the eyes with grief and chilling the heart.

On this side, they go to dance halls and theaters seeking pleasure, spending thousands of gold coins without hesitation.

On that side, cries shake the earth with broken hearts, and they are helplessly unable to reverse their fate.

I urge you all to show compassion and quickly donate from your wealth to help the disaster victims.

Within the four seas, we are all brothers and sisters; how can we sit idly by and watch them die?

If only we save what we waste in a single day, the lives of millions can be preserved.

National Studies

Miss Wang Bingmei's Tang Poetry

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Su Wu Temple - Wen Tingyun

Su Wu's spirit fades before the Han envoy,

Ancient temple, tall trees, rain hazy.

Wild geese lost beyond the clouds, barbarian sky's moon,

Sheep return on the slopes, frontier grass in smoke.

Distant palace towers not a jade pavilion,

When he left, his cap and sword marked youthful years.

Maoling sees no title-bestowing seal,

Only to autumn waves, weep for the departed stream.

Palace Poem - Xue Feng

In twelve towers, all adorn themselves at dawn,

Gazing at the Emperor from the Tower of Wishing for Immortals.

Fragrant-extinguishing golden beast, chains cold,

Water drips from copper dragon, the daytime clock ticks long.

Cloud-like hair done, still facing the mirror,

Silken robe wanting to change, adding more fragrance.

Peeking from afar, the main hall just opening,

Robes and trousers, palace maids sweep the imperial bed.

Poor Girl - Qin Taoyu

A humble door, never knowing silk and perfume,

Intending to rely on a good matchmaker, yet lamenting herself.

Who loves a refined and elegant demeanor?

All pity her thrifty dress in these times.

Daring to boast of skillful needlework,

Not competing to draw long eyebrows.

Bitterly hating pressing gold thread year after year,

Making wedding clothes for others.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

Hollywood Stars' Villas and Estates with "For Rent" Signs

— Mi Qi

Moving from a large house to a small house, subdividing small houses for rent, turning one family into two, and two into three. This was the housing situation after the January 28th Incident in Shanghai due to economic decline. However, the current economic decline is widespread throughout the world, and Hollywood is no exception. As a result, Hollywood stars are putting their residences, villas, and estates up for rent. Not only are past stars, due to economic hardship and to save expenses, forced to let people live in their mansions, but even current stars, who own one residence in the east and one villa in the west, are compelled to part with some, keeping their Hollywood houses for themselves and renting out the houses in more remote locations to others. Isn't this the same as ordinary people, after suffering financial setbacks, renting out the remaining rooms to others? Before the economic decline, they used to live in Hollywood town on weekdays, at the seaside on weekends, and in estates during holidays. Each location had enormous garages, stables, swimming pools, tennis courts, flower gardens, exercise rooms, theaters, and everything else imaginable, enjoying the blessings of life to the fullest. Money was of no concern, so how could there be any reason to part with and rent them out? Now, since the wave of bank collapses the year before last, hungry wolves are at their doors, poised to enter their homes. Even those who aren't worried about their finances, seeing others downsizing and economizing on daily expenses, dare not flaunt their luxury. Now, let's talk about a few large houses and estates of stars that are now displaying "For Rent" signs.

Marion Davies has a villa on the Santa Monica beach, facing the Pacific Ocean. That villa is merely her "guest house," so of course, in terms of formality and luxury, it cannot compare to her residence in Santa Monica, but it already has twelve bedrooms, six bathrooms, and servants' quarters. The interior is decorated with foreign antiques, making it quite serene and pleasant. Previously, Beryl Burke lived there, paying a monthly rent of $2,500 USD. Now, Marlene Dietrich lives there, paying a monthly rent of only $1,500 USD. Bebe Daniels has become a well-known landlady in Hollywood. She has three houses for rent by the sea. The most expensive is $1,000 USD per month, which Pola Negri used to live in. The interior is extremely luxurious, with a private beach in front. Mary Pickford, everyone knows her Pickfair Mansion, which she and Douglas Fairbanks built together, is a world-famous place, but her villa by the sea is now also displaying a "For Rent" sign. If you are willing to have this American sweetheart as your landlady, paying a monthly rent of $600 USD can be considered inexpensive. It is also built on a private beach.

Norma Talmadge was the most beautiful red star in Hollywood ten years ago. She now also has a seaside villa for rent. In addition to the endless Pacific Ocean for swimming, there is also a freshwater swimming pool, and the rent is only $850 USD per month. Sylvia Sidney is currently living in a house rented from Richard Barthelmess. It is also by the sea, making it ideal for summer retreats. Now that winter has arrived, she is living in Hollywood town and is even considering renting out half of that large house. Lilian Harvey, after moving down from the hills, had her house rented by Myrna Loy. But Myrna Loy is now moving out. If you are willing, just pay a monthly rent of $750 USD. That is very cheap, because that house is built in the Spanish style, with a garden surrounding the house, and the design is extremely ingenious. The furniture inside is all imported from France, which can be said to be exquisitely crafted. In particular, there is a game room with everything from billiards to ping-pong. Colleen Moore's beautiful residence built in Bel Air is now also rented to Marlene Dietrich for a monthly rent of $1,250 USD. The above are just a few examples. The rest need not be listed one by one.

Reader Opinions

My Review of "Bai Hua Zhou"

— Fei Nianzu

Undoubtedly, this film is another work similar to "Hong Lou Chun Shen" and "Chun Xiao Qu," still an old tune of love entanglement.

The director of this film, Wen Yimin, seems to lack skill in handling the technical aspects and acting, especially in the portrayal of the characters' personalities, which reveals a major shortcoming. For example, Chen Yumei's engagement in children's education is only written as being due to love entanglements and misunderstandings. The sudden transformation of Ye Qiuxin is also written illogically. Other aspects, such as Yu Guang's inconsistency and Ye Qiuxin's violent attitude, all demonstrate the director's immature skills.

As for the actors, Chen Yumei is still competent, but there has not been much progress compared to before. Ye Qiuxin also fails to give us a better impression. Chen Qixia is passable. Yu Guang and Li Ying are mediocre.

Finally, I think it is worth mentioning that the playwright has at least made some progress compared to "Hong Lou Chun Shen," because in "Bai Hua Zhou," in addition to love entanglements, he has also added some significance of serving society.

Impressions of "Shanghai 24 Hours"

— Wu Sheng

When I saw Shen Xiling's "Shanghai 24 Hours," following "Women's Cry," at the New Light Grand Theater, my soul was deeply moved. Really, at that time, my blood vessels almost burst open.

Clearly, the subject matter of this film is extremely realistic, and the images are stimulating and touching. It depicts the general population living in rural areas who, due to rural bankruptcy, cannot survive and yearn for the superficial prosperity of the city. True, the front of the city is beautiful and splendid, but the back of the city is dark and cruel. The playwright of this film wanted to show the darkness behind the city within 24 hours, the bloody and blurred misery suppressed under the luxurious and licentious life, to let those who yearn for the city know. However, because the whole play was affected by the environment, it changed its original appearance. Therefore, in terms of content and dramatic power, it is loose and has a sense of fragmentation!

The director's use of techniques is commendable. As for the actors' performances, I personally think that Zhao Dan's Old Zhao is the best, and Chen Ningqiu's Chen Da and Zhou Boxun's compradore are also quite competent.

The scenery is very realistic, and the lighting seems a little dim.

The Star Film Company's new film "Bigamy," directed by Wu Cun, starring Gao Zhanfei, Yan Yuexian, and Gao Fuping, is scheduled to premiere at the New Light Theater on the 21st of this month.

Review of "Peach and Plum Calamity"

— Zhang Dahui

The author tells us here a very sad and tragic story. In this story, there is a major social problem. A young man who can endure hardship is made unemployed and suffers such a cruel ending for the sake of "justice" and "humanity." Undoubtedly, this is a film with social significance.

The director's technique is indeed not bad, and there are many clever touches. He can fully expose the real phenomena of society, such as the fact that there are hundreds of applicants for a single employee position. There are all kinds of despicable and filthy things in the hotel. Jianping's tearing up of his diploma shows that diplomas are deceptive waste that cannot be exchanged for food. The actors' expressions are very profound, especially Yuan Muzhi and Chen Boer. For directors and actors who have always been engaged in stage plays to have such achievements when they first set foot on the screen is indeed surprising and considered quite satisfactory.

But there are also a few minor flaws: the pronunciation is not very clear in some places. Why did Jianping not have shackles on his hands and feet in prison? The final subtitles are superfluous and do not conform to the meaning of the play. This is probably not the original intention of the playwright!

Wallace Beery, Jackie Cooper, and Robert Young in a Joint Production of "Treasure Island"

— Yun Men

Nineteenth-century romantic literature specializes in depicting martial arts, adventure, love, etc. The great writer Robert Louis Stevenson was the last writer of this style and a landmark separating the artistic trends of the nineteenth and twentieth centuries. As for her poetic talent, it has long been recognized by the world, and her most famous and popular representative novel is "Treasure Island," which is currently being screened in Nanjing. This book has been translated into dozens of languages and is a must-read for those who love literature. Even Mr. Lin Shu Qinnan of our country, in addition to Charles Dickens' novels, also translated this book into "Treasure Island," making it a most popular work.

MGM produced this film at a cost of over a million US dollars. The selection of characters in the film was also painstakingly managed. Wallace Beery, the protagonist of "Viva Villa!", will play Long John Silver, child prodigy Jackie Cooper will play Jim Hawkins, Lionel Barrymore will play the mad Captain, Lewis Stone will play Captain Smollett, and Hessel will play the weird Ben Gunn. Undoubtedly, their talents will not disappoint. As for the background, dialogue, mood, etc., MGM's reputation is sufficient to guarantee it. The Christmas holiday is here, and here is the most wonderful and richest gift contributed by the eighth art.

Movie Chatter

Jean Harlow will co-star in a new film with Charles Laughton and Charles Boyer, titled "Peacock Feathers."

"Divorce" will be remade into a talkie, starring George Arliss and Janet Gaynor.

Wang Ying returned to Shanghai from Japan the day before yesterday, but it is said that he has not yet joined Yihua Film Company.

Recently, several foreigners of American and French nationality in Shanghai plan to cooperate with Chinese film companies to raise funds to produce a "standard" Chinese sound film to promote the international market. They have specially invited the world-renowned musician Freeman, who is currently in Shanghai, to compose the music. They claim that they are absolutely certain that the business will be profitable, but this is another means for foreign capital to control the Chinese film production industry. However, it is not known whether the Chinese film company authorities will be lured by them.

The first work of Diantong Film Company, "Peach and Plum Calamity," was sent to Nanjing for inspection the other day. It is said that five sections will be deleted.

Respectfully Dedicating "Bigamy" to Urban Youths

— Fire

"Bigamy" is Wu Cun's first concentrated effort since joining Star Film Company. It is also the first collaborative crystallization of the couple Gao Zhanfei and Gao Qianping. Of course, this is an unprecedented masterpiece that every movie fan must pay attention to.

The content of the film depicts an old farmer who drinks the bitter wine of life and works hard all his life, sending his son to the city to study, hoping that he can get an official position. Who knew that this youth was infected with the bad habits of the city, leisurely enjoying himself all day long, drinking deeply from the sweet cup of love. The life of poverty and wealth between father and son is like a world of difference. This is a sketch of a family tragedy and a silhouette of a social tragedy. It has faithful satire and warm exhortations for the frivolous youth of the city. I respectfully dedicate this film to you - the urban youth. The film is scheduled to be shown at the New Light Grand Theater tonight at 9:15.

A Scene from "Bigamy"

— Fire

In Wu Cun's directed film "Bigamy," there is a subtitle that reads: "There are many sham schools in Shanghai, and these schools have unknowingly buried many promising youths."

Gao Zhanfei in "Bigamy" is a truly promising youth, but after he went to university in Shanghai, he was infected with the bad habits of the city and became a frivolous youth.

Every day, when the brilliant night market opened, he put on a handsome suit and secretly climbed out of the school walls with two or three classmates to go dancing. One night, when they returned from dancing, it happened to be raining heavily. In an instant, everyone was drenched, and they climbed back into the school from the walls in a panic. One of the classmates accidentally lost his footing and fell into a water tank at the foot of the wall, and everyone burst into laughter. At this time, those teachers who only took dry salaries were in their gentle homes. And these youths were buried by them in this way. (Editor's Note)

Collection of Short Comments

— Lin Qin

(1)

Many people can't even distinguish the nationality of the world's great writers, yet they still talk about world literature. Are they deceiving the living or cheating the dead?

(2)

To scold someone is considered the most glorious thing in some people's hearts. In fact, the words they use to scold others fit them perfectly.

(3)

I think the duty of a publicist is to promote their own company, but no one told you to specifically sabotage other companies. It seems that the current publicists are specialized in sabotage work.

(4)

What Clara Bow said... what Greta Garbo did, these are all facts idealized by great writers. They didn't personally hear Clara Bow say anything, and they wouldn't translate it from old foreign magazines because they don't understand foreign languages!

(5)

Take a paragraph from a foreign article, write your own name on it, and consider it your own work. Great film theorist!

Submission Guidelines for Shen Bao Movie Special

This publication is a film publication that assists cultural promotion and artistic expression. We welcome external contributions. Once published, generous compensation will be provided.

Once a submitted article is published and compensated, the copyright belongs to Shen Bao.

This publication mainly uses vernacular Chinese and must use new-style punctuation.

When submitting an article, each article must be stamped with a seal; otherwise, it will be considered a rejection.

If the submission is a translation, the original work should be attached. Mixed use of English can be reduced where possible.

Unless otherwise stated in advance and return postage is included, the publication is not responsible for the preservation or return of manuscripts, photos, etc.

Submissions sent to multiple publications, plagiarized text, or verbatim descriptions will not be compensated if discovered.

Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper or write horizontally, and do not use a pencil.

Due to limited space in this publication, the text should be as concise as possible. Each manuscript should be around 500 words.

The film novel "Jin Lian Jie" will be temporarily suspended for one day due to the non-arrival of the next installment.
